Yongding and Hutuo Rivers Both Overflow; Dredging of the Southern Grand Canal Completed and Water Released 17

(Tianjin) The water level of the Yongding River in the Wuqing section has risen again, with many breaches along the river embankments. The Yubakou and Shuangkou sections north of Tianjin are overflowing the top of the embankments. More than a thousand people from over thirty villages in Pangzhuang are desperately trying to block the breaches. However, due to the rapid and large flow of water, they were unable to protect it in time, and the embankment collapsed for more than ten zhang (approximately 33 meters). More than twenty villages, including Chenzuizi and Qujiadian, were submerged, covering more than one hundred square li (approximately 50 square kilometers). The North Grand Canal Bureau is coordinating with the Yongding River Bureau to intensify rescue efforts. The upstream water level of the Hutuo River has risen sharply. It overflowed in Xuzhao Village, Anping, on the 13th. Villagers are sounding gongs day and night to protect the area. More than a thousand mu (approximately 67 hectares) of crops along the embankments have been flooded. (Special dispatch, 16th)

(Tianjin) The dredging of the South Grand Canal has been completed, and water was released at 1:00 a.m. on the 16th. Secretary-General Ma Yanchong of the Municipal Government, as well as over a hundred gentry and merchants, attended. Chairman Li Tingyu of the Dredging Committee delivered a speech. The project cost 300,000 yuan, which was used to dredge the river in sections, and was completed in two months. Water conservancy in the suburbs of Tianjin will be convenient from now on. Today, when the water was released, Li Tingyu wrote a couplet himself and hung it on the platform: "If the dredge takes even half a penny of graft, though spared by heaven's punishment today, he will surely fall into the river and die." The water release coincided with the Lesser Heat solar term. Thinking of this matter relying on the strength of the people, ask who will compete with you for credit? (Special dispatch, 16th)

(Tianjin) Liu Yufu, Director of the Yongding River Bureau, came to Tianjin to meet with the North China Water Conservancy Association to discuss the dangerous situation of the southern embankment. (Special dispatch, 16th)

Montreux Conference: British-Russian Dispute Resolved - Straits Navigation Method Determined - New Convention Can Be Signed in Geneva 28

Montreux - The Montreux Conference on the Dardanelles Strait has passed the Soviet amendment to the British draft regarding the need for the Straits in wartime. There were no objections. The final obstacle to the negotiations has now been removed as a result. It is said that the amendment that has now been passed is that warships of belligerent countries may not pass through the Straits, except for those fulfilling obligations under the League of Nations Covenant and those involving Turkey as a party to the agreement in certain situations. (Reuters dispatch, 15th)

Montreux - Since the Montreux Conference passed the Soviet amendment, the main point of contention has been resolved. The only remaining matters to be discussed are decisive issues, which should not be difficult to resolve. Representatives of all concerned countries may sign the new convention on Monday of next week and announce the closure of the conference. As for the unresolved decisive issues, there are three: (1) the issue of the survival of the Straits Management Committee. The Turkish government originally requested its abolition, and the United Kingdom is expected to agree. (2) The issue of aircraft of various countries flying over Turkish airspace. Turkey originally requested a ban, but because of the strong opposition from France and the United Kingdom, some concessions may be made so that the conference can adopt a compromise approach, namely, prohibiting aircraft from various countries from flying over military areas. (3) The Japanese amendment, which argues that the measures that the ten countries may take in accordance with Article 16 of the League of Nations Covenant should be implemented only after the League of Nations Council has approved them with a two-thirds majority vote and the majority of the signatory countries of the new convention have also endorsed them. The conference has already satisfied this point in principle yesterday and is unlikely to cause disagreement again. (Havas dispatch, 16th)

Main Issues of the Montreux Conference Resolved: British Concessions Praised by Various Countries 29

Montreux - Since the Montreux Conference reconvened on the 6th of this month, the United Kingdom and Russia have been arguing for many days over the issue of warships of various countries passing through the Straits in wartime without a resolution. It was not until the afternoon of today that the Montreux Conference passed the Soviet amendment, and the points of contention between the United Kingdom and Russia were swept away. It is generally expected that the new convention can be signed at the end of this week or the beginning of next week. From then on, merchant ships of all countries, whether in war or peacetime, will be free to pass through the Straits. The French navy will also be able to obtain coal oil from Russia and Romania. It is also unknown whether France and Turkey will conclude a mutual assistance convention, as in the cases of the Franco-Russian Mutual Assistance Convention and the Balkan Entente. From this, it can be seen that the claims of France, Russia, and Romania have been victorious. As for the United Kingdom, its conciliatory attitude this time has been praised by the various delegations. The country had already made as many concessions as possible to the demands of other delegations. In addition, because the Russian Foreign Minister, Litvinov, insisted firmly, it became clear that the issue of blockading the Black Sea in wartime was a key point in Russia's plan and should be adhered to and never conceded. Therefore, [the UK] was unwilling to jeopardize the conference due to this dispute. And because there were many international conferences that ended in failure, if the Montreux Conference were to repeat the same mistake, or even if it did not fail but was postponed, it would be tantamount to a mental defeat for the countries that were loyal to the international rule of law. Therefore, [the UK] sacrificed itself and showed compromise to take care of the overall situation. When the vote was taken today, Romanian Foreign Minister Titulescu had not returned home, so he did not vote. Japan and Yugoslavia had suggested to their respective governments that they support the Russian claim, but they still wanted to submit the full text of the Russian amendment to their respective governments for review, so they both abstained from voting. (Havas dispatch, 15th)

Montreux - When the Montreux Conference voted on the Soviet amendment yesterday, the representatives of Japan and Yugoslavia both abstained from voting because they had to consult their respective governments. The Japanese delegation then submitted an amendment, which the conference immediately referred to the drafting committee for discussion in order to find a solution that would satisfy Japan and remove the difficulties that the Japanese amendment might cause in practice. (Havas dispatch, 17th)

Montreux - The Soviet amendment has been passed by the Montreux Conference. When the vote was taken, Romanian Foreign Minister Titulescu did not participate in the vote because he had already returned to his country, but the Romanian government has recently sent a telegram expressing its approval. Titulescu himself does not intend to come again because the conference is proceeding smoothly. As for the attitude of the Yugoslav government, it is still unknown. Observers believe that the Soviet amendment does not threaten the security of the Balkan Entente countries, and Yugoslavia will certainly express its approval. In addition, although Bulgaria had taken a reserved attitude on this matter, Yugoslavia had soothed it, and it is now expressing satisfaction. (Havas dispatch, 16th)

Mussolini's Speech: All Nations Have Raised the White Flag; Italy Commemorates the End of Sanctions 34

He said, "Today is July 15th. All the nations around the world that participated in the sanctions against Italy have raised the white flag of truce on the ramparts of their sanction barriers. What we see here is not only a sign of surrender but also a sign of the restoration of common sense. Moreover, Italy's economic victory this time is due to the efforts of all the people, young and old, male and female, who contributed to it. When the sanctions were implemented, our people did not panic or tremble, nor did they lose heart. Instead, they all prepared to sacrifice, because everyone held a belief that civilization and justice would ultimately prevail in both Europe and Africa." Although the speech was brief, the audience cheered enthusiastically. The Prime Minister repeatedly appeared on the balcony to thank the crowds. (Havas Dispatch, July 15)

British Minister of Commerce Announces Progress in Various Industries; Sanctions Against Italy Resulted in a Loss of Four Million Pounds; Negotiations Are Underway to Restore Trade to Previous Levels 35

(London) Minister of Commerce Runciman announced the recent commercial situation of Britain in the House of Commons today, stating that if there are no major developments overseas and if industrial peace in Britain can remain unchanged for a long time, then the progress made in the past few years has a great hope of continuing. British commercial policy remains unchanged, based on equal opportunities for all countries, but it will only be effective if all countries fulfill their responsibilities. Now, the unnatural restrictions and cumbersome examples that hinder multilateral international trade must be removed before the overseas trade that Britain enjoyed before the crisis of 1931 can gradually recover. The policy of developing overseas markets through commercial agreements is actively underway. In the coming period, British exporters' hopes will largely be focused on the continued expansion of intra-imperial trade and increased trade with the Sterling Area countries. However, looking at the global situation, there are still some exciting features. Statistics from the past few years have made us realize that although economic nationalism is growing daily, the prosperity of various countries rises and falls together. However, what is certain is that the progress of the gold bloc countries is still being hampered by special factors. Runciman then detailed the significant progress made by various major British industries in the past year, except for cotton and coal, stating that industries supplying the domestic market have made good progress in recent years, but export trade has progressed very slowly. Runciman then cited various statistics to prove the increase in the country's economic position, estimating that in June of this year, the number of insured unemployed who found work, excluding farmers, increased by 440,000 compared to a year ago, and the number of unemployed has decreased by 300,000. Although railway transportation faces competition from road transportation, the revenue for the first six months of this year increased by 1.83 million pounds compared to the same period last year, almost all of which was from freight revenue. Postal revenue also increased by 4% in six months. Retail sales best reflect the national situation, increasing by 6% in 1935 compared to the previous year, and continued to develop this year, with the value of goods in the first five months of this year increasing by 7.5% compared to 1935. Industrial products exported and sold domestically last year increased by 7% compared to 1934, and the first quarter of this year increased by 9% compared to the first quarter of last year. The merchant ships under construction at the end of June totaled 850,000 gross tons, compared to only 560,000 gross tons a year ago. Runciman continued, stating that sanctions against Italy caused Britain to lose 4 million pounds in exports to Italy in the first half of this year, but it is expected that it will be restored soon. The British authorities are in close contact with the Italian authorities to eliminate the obstacles to British trade with Italy as soon as possible. Runciman then described the situation of various major industries, stating that engineering continues to show signs of improvement, and there are several types, such as machine tools, where demand exceeds supply. Regarding electrical engineering, all aspects have continued to increase since 1935. The activity of various other industries can be seen from the huge demand for light and heavy electrical materials. The automobile industry also continues to thrive. From October last year to April this year, the production of passenger cars and chassis increased by more than 11% compared to the same period last year, while commercial vehicles increased by 10%. Although rayon is still a nascent industry, it has developed rapidly. Britain is now the largest producer of rayon yarn, and the export of rayon fabrics also ranks second in the world. The increase in sales of rayon does not hinder other textile industries but instead provides a valuable source of new raw materials for various textile industries. Runciman then analyzed the figures for overseas trade in the first half of this year, saying that although the increase in export trade in the first six months of 1936 compared to 1935 was not as rapid as in recent years, it still increased. The total value of exports from January to June 1935 was 206,500,000 pounds, which increased to 207,900,000 pounds in the same period this year. The increase in imports was even greater than that in exports. The import of food, beverages, and tobacco increased from 166,000,000 pounds to 179,000,000 pounds, while raw materials and unfinished goods increased from 103,000,000 pounds to 119,000,000 pounds, and finished or mostly finished goods increased from about 88,000,000 pounds to 101,000,000 pounds. Although exports only increased by 1,400,000 pounds, it should not be considered entirely unfavorable. The reason for the slow increase is partly due to the temporary complete cessation of export trade to Italy, which decreased by 4,000,000 pounds compared to the first half of last year. Although the trade deficit increased from 124,000,000 pounds to 162,000,000 pounds, it is not possible to predict any serious unfavorable balance of payments this year. The decline in international trade seems to have stopped and has slightly improved. Britain's position in world trade has clearly increased. In 1932, Britain accounted for 9.9% of world export trade, which increased to 10.8% in 1935. (Reuters, July 15)

Attempted Assassination of British Monarch; Gun Falls to Ground; Assailant Arrested 36

(London) King Edward VIII, accompanied by his brother, the Duke of York, was returning to the palace from Hyde Park today when an unidentified assailant, intending to assassinate the King, attempted to fire a gun near the park. He was apprehended by police guarding the route, preventing him from firing the weapon. The King remained unharmed. The suspect is currently being interrogated by Scotland Yard. (National Telegram, July 16)

(London) Today, while King Edward VIII was riding from Buckingham Palace to Hyde Park to present colors to the Guards, an attempt was made to assassinate him. Fortunately, the handgun the assailant was holding was struck down just as he was aiming to fire. Four of the five chambers in the gun were loaded. The incident occurred near the Wellington Arch on Constitution Hill. The assailant, a British man, pushed through the crowd to the front row, and just as he was about to raise the gun, it was knocked out of his hand. The crowd surged forward, and the assailant turned to flee but was eventually exhausted and arrested. He was immediately taken to Hyde Park Police Station. The bullets in his gun were not fired. The man, wearing brown trousers and a collar, trembled violently after being captured. He has a disability in one foot and wears specially made leather boots. He has now been identified as George Andrew McMahon and will be arraigned this afternoon at Bow Street Magistrates' Court, where he is expected to be remanded for a week for further investigation. The suspect is charged with illegally carrying a weapon with intent to endanger life. Detectives presented the recovered handgun, discovering that four of its five chambers were loaded, with only the topmost chamber empty. According to his statement to detectives, "This is all the fault of Home Secretary Sir John Simon. I sent him a letter last night and spoke to him on the phone this morning. The King will not be harmed in any way. I had no intention of hurting him; I am only expressing a protest." This shocking incident, which has shaken the entire country, was witnessed by the Duke of York, who was riding behind the King as his personal aide-de-camp. Witnesses present at the scene all stated that the King remained very calm and his horse maintained its original speed. The King calmly looked around at the scene. The King and the Duke of York did not change their schedule for the day due to the incident. (Reuters, July 16)

(London) Today, King Edward VIII, accompanied by his brother, the Duke of York, was riding from Buckingham Palace when a shocking incident occurred at a corner in Hyde Park. A man attempted to break through the crowd lining the route and take action, but he was stopped on the spot and arrested. A handgun was found on the scene. The man will be prosecuted for political crimes. The King was not alarmed by the incident and proceeded as usual to Hyde Park, where he addressed the assembled guards, saying, "Humanity is now yearning for peace. Perhaps only a few of us gathered here this morning can truly understand the horrors of the World War twenty years ago. Though it contained much suffering, it was also filled with a spirit of mutual aid. It is my sincere hope and prayer that we will never again see such terrible times in our era. Humanity is now yearning for peace. In these peaceful days, you will find opportunities for fulfilling your duties and serving others, which are no less noble than what was demonstrated on the battlefield in the past." The ceremony took place in clear weather with bright sunshine. The new colors were received by the first and second battalions of the Grenadier Guards, the second and third battalions of the Coldstream Guards, and the second battalion of the Scots Guards. Cheering crowds stood along the route to watch the King and his brother, the Duke of York, ride to the parade ground. Queen Mary and other noble ladies also attended the ceremony. (Reuters, July 16)

(London) After a short stay at Buckingham Palace, the King traveled by car to St. James's Palace to review official documents. He then traveled by car to Belverdere Fort Villa to play golf. According to witnesses at the Wellington Arch, a mounted policeman's horse seemed to obstruct the assassin's view. While the assassin hesitated, his gun was knocked from his hand by a policeman and a woman standing nearby. The King's expression seemed to suddenly turn serious, and he turned his head to look at the people, seemingly searching for his equerry, Sir Aird. Sir Aird, who was riding behind with Lieutenant General White Rock, immediately returned to the scene and spoke to a policeman. A woman who was standing near the assassin said that the assassin seemed to have pushed forward from the fourth row behind us to the edge of the sidewalk. I heard someone shout, "Catch him, catch him!" As the assassin tried to break through the police cordon, a woman followed him. At the same time, the woman and the policeman knocked the gun from his hand onto the road. Another person said that when the assassin took out the gun, someone shouted and surrounded him. Just as the assassin was about to raise his gun, a policeman pushed his arm up, and then the surrounding crowd attacked him and threw him to the ground. Several officers of the Guards of the Duke of York also saw the whole incident. The Duke of York and the King were both unperturbed. When the assassin, McMahon, was arrested on the spot, another person rushed in front of the police and started a fight. That person was also arrested. Two women who witnessed the incident were taken to police headquarters in a police car. According to a photograph taken by a reporter, the assassin was being taken into an ambulance by three policemen. (Reuters, July 16)

(London) Police authorities issued a statement at 2:40 PM today, saying, "This morning, after the King presided over the flag-raising ceremony in Hyde Park, he immediately rode towards Buckingham Palace. When he reached near the Wellington Arch, a person suddenly jumped out of the crowd. The subsequent details are unclear, but a handgun, loaded with four bullets, fell to the ground between the King and his guards. No shots were heard. The police immediately arrested the person." (Havas Dispatch, July 16)

(London) The assailant who attempted to harm the King is British. His name is McMahon. (Havas News Agency, July 16)

(London) Home Secretary Simon made a statement in the House of Commons this afternoon regarding the incident involving the King. He first responded to a question from Labour MP Attlee, asking whether the Home Secretary could make a statement on the matter. Simon replied in a serious tone, saying, "This morning, as the King's entourage was returning to the palace from the flag-raising ceremony in Hyde Park, a person emerged from the crowd near the Wellington Arch on Constitution Hill and alarmed the royal entourage. The House of Commons is undoubtedly shocked by this news. The exact details of what happened are still unclear, but a handgun fell between the King and his accompanying soldiers. The person has been arrested and taken to Hyde Park Police Station. He did not fire the weapon, but the gun contained four bullets in its five chambers. The person will be arraigned at Bow Street Police Station this afternoon and is expected to be detained. The entire House is extremely grateful to God that the King escaped unharmed." (Reuters, July 16)

Where Is the Hirota Cabinet Going? (1) 38

— Jia He

People call the Hirota Cabinet, which was appointed to form a cabinet, the "First Hirota Cabinet"; the cabinet that was interfered with by the military and changed its cabinet-forming policy is called the "Second Hirota Cabinet." If the above names are correct, then the Hirota Cabinet after the "Special Diet" should be called the "Third Hirota Cabinet." Because, "The mission of the First Cabinet was to purge the military internally and coordinate internationally, full of liberal colors, and the cabinet-forming staff was still the son-in-law of the quasi-elder Makino Nobuaki, and the current ambassador to the UK, Yoshida Shigeru. The Second Cabinet" was clearly constrained by the Army's deployment of the "military attache system" as a legitimate tactic. It abandoned liberal cabinet members, excluded political parties from occupying the Ministry of Home Affairs, and even made a secret oral agreement with the Army: to reform the political structure, to further control various industrial sectors, to increase the authority of the cabinet investigation bureau, which is the Army's tool cabinet, to expand armaments without limit, and to establish active autonomous diplomacy; as for the issue of military purge, that is the Army's internal affair and has nothing to do with outsiders. A cabinet of this nature, called "a new era for all government affairs, is essentially a radical fascist regime. If Hirota could carry it out one by one, then the "February 26th" coup would not have failed, but would have succeeded, because the souls of Shiro Nonaka and others are entirely attached to Hirota Koki. Naturally, that is absolutely impossible. The occurrence of the "February 26th" coup has its historical nature; the failure of the coup also lacks the objective conditions for success. If there is no objective need for the rise of radical fascism, even if the young military officers of Miyakesaka have the ability to move mountains and overturn seas, they will be powerless. Therefore, denying the actions of the "Second Cabinet" is an inevitable scene.

Since Hirota's mission to power was to continue to carry out the unfinished tasks of the Okada Cabinet, why did he make an oral agreement with the military? The reason is very simple: according to regulations, the Minister of the Army is a military officer. In the past, no matter which prime minister could recommend a responsible person from the military other than a military officer, and Hirota was naturally no exception. Furthermore, according to precedent, the Minister of the Army was not something that the Prime Minister could freely recommend; it was always decided by the Chief of the General Staff, the Inspector General of Military Education, and the previous Minister of the Army, the so-called three chiefs of the Army, and then submitted to the Emperor for appointment. Hirota after the coup could not even think about breaking this precedent. Under the above premise, Hirota's cabinet, who would rather pull in Terauchi Juichi than listen to Araki Sadao and others, it cannot be said that this was his intelligence. Because General Terauchi is not only the descendant of Terauchi Masatake, the so-called leader of the long-standing faction within the Army, but also a count with great skills in maneuvering. In the camp of the Kansai financial clique, he, together with Generals Ugaki Kazushige and Abe Nobuyuki, can obtain equal votes of confidence. Secondly, in Hirota's view, the political skills of the young military officers were quite naive. Bearing the responsibility for the coup that disturbed the Emperor, they did not strive to clear their names but only focused on making an oral agreement to form a cabinet, leaving the difficulties of the special Diet behind. They did not know that since parliamentary politics cannot be closed, the power of the parliament can not only direct the cabinet but also control the military. Making an oral agreement is secret, but there are public opportunities to deny the oral agreement, so what is Hirota afraid of? Thirdly, the constitution states that the military cannot directly interfere in politics. If the military wants to fulfill the requested oral agreement, it can only take indirect means. The young military officers also understand this very well. Therefore, their friendship with Hirota led to the expansion of the authority of the Cabinet Investigation Bureau into a small cabinet within the cabinet, and the chief, Yoshida Shigeru (a different person from the current ambassador to the UK), was promoted to Minister without Portfolio. However, Hirota did not have this power and should wait for a cabinet decision. The cabinet decision was made after the cabinet was formed. Before the cabinet was formed, the current problem was not to fulfill the demands of the military but that the military and Hirota were busy dealing with the special Diet. The special Diet has such power, not only because it holds a written constitution, but because the economic center of Japan is in the hands of the bourgeoisie. (Landlords and nobles have become bourgeois since the Southwest War. Only those who are ignorant of Japanese history believe that Japan still has a huge feudal force. They regard the military as a feudal force, as a feudal force that can resist the propertied class, which is also wrong. Because the divisions within the Army and Navy are a reflection of the propertied class fighting secretly for profit. The remaining feudal forces are not enough to influence the entire political situation in Japan.) On the eve of the Meiji Restoration, the anger of Osaka merchants changed the colors of the daimyo (feudal lords). Not to mention the power of Mitsui, Mitsubishi, Sumitomo, and Yasuda today is a thousand times greater than the "kuramoto" and "zakahai" of the past, and even the "Konoike of the world" is more雄大万倍; and the leaders of the military are not enough to be compared with the feudal daimyo. For the above-mentioned reasons, Hirota dared to make an oral agreement with Terauchi to overcome the difficulties of forming a cabinet.

President of the Soviet Academy of Sciences, Karpinsky, Passes Away 41

(Moscow) Karpinsky, President of the Soviet Academy of Sciences, passed away today at the age of 90. Karpinsky was the son of a coal mine engineer and graduated from the Engineering Department of the University of St. Petersburg in 1866. In 1877, he was selected as a professor of geology, and in 1885, he was appointed as the chairman of the Geological Committee. Karpinsky had been working at the Soviet Academy of Sciences for 50 years. In the past 20 years, Karpinsky had been continuously elected as the president of the Academy and served as an advisor to foreign research institutions. Karpinsky was a pioneer of Soviet geology and had written more than 300 books on geology, which were widely sold in the European part of the Soviet Union. Karpinsky devoted his research to the construction of socialism, making many contributions and being very popular among the working masses. In 1935, Karpinsky was elected as a member of the Soviet Central Executive Committee. (TASS, 15th)

Increased Destroyer Proposal: Britain Notifies the US and Japan of the London Treaty's "Escalator Clause" 43

(London) Britain has formally invoked the "escalator clause" of the 1930 London Naval Treaty in order to retain 40,000 tons of overage destroyers that should be scrapped by the end of the year. The British government sent this document to the US and Japanese ambassadors last night to convey it to their respective governments. Naval experts today believe that recent foreign naval developments make it necessary for Britain to invoke this clause. According to the clause, any signatory country that believes its national security is seriously threatened by the construction of new ships by non-signatory countries may increase its tonnage after notifying other signatory countries, and other signatory countries may also make proportional increases. The issue of retaining the Hawkins-class cruisers is still under discussion by the British, Japanese, and American governments. It is heard that the British government has sent another note to the Japanese and American ambassadors regarding this issue. These cruisers are the Hawkins (9,800 tons), the Effingham (9,770 tons), and the Frobisher (9,860 tons). The British government plans to改造or re-equip these three ships. (Reuters, 16th)

(Washington) Since the British government notified the US and Japan that it had decided to invoke Article 21, the "escalator" clauses of the London Naval Treaty, in order to preserve 190,000 tons of destroyers, the US government should follow suit and additionally preserve 40,000 tons of destroyers in order to seek reciprocity. Regarding this, naval figures found it strange that the British government's announcement did not mention the issue of cruiser tonnage, which was inconsistent with the announcement made in May of this year, but they still praised it, saying that this move could provide a solution to the issue of additional destroyer tonnage preservation without any ambiguity. (Havas, 15th)

(Tokyo) Britain has decided to retain an overage of 40,000 tons of destroyers and has notified Japan and the United States of its intention to invoke the escalation clause. However, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs has not yet received this telegram. It may arrive in the near future, and at that time, after the contents of the British notification are transferred to the two overseas provinces for consultation, a reply can be given. Japan has largely understood Britain's request. It is confirmed that Japan's fundamental position is as follows:

(1) If Britain invokes the escalation clause, the corresponding ship type that Japan should obtain does not have a corresponding treaty overage for retaining destroyers, so it can obtain a submarine tonnage.

(2) Although Japan maintains its current submarine tonnage, the London Treaty expires at the end of this year, so it is more in line with the spirit of naval arms reduction to maintain old ships rather than build new ones.

(3) Moreover, although Japan retains its destroyers and submarines that should be scrapped, they are mostly old ships, so they will not pose a threat to Britain and the United States.

(4) Britain believes that maintaining the Hawkins-class cruisers should not be considered a violation of the treaty. However, regarding the interpretation of Article 19 of the London Treaty, in the exchange of official documents between Britain, Japan, and the United States, cruisers are divided into ship types and ship classes, and there is a clear distinction between A-class and B-class. Therefore, Britain's claim to apply A-class to B-class as the same ship type is a violation of the treaty. (Domei, 16th)

A Travelogue of Japan (3) 58

— By Our Reporters, Hu Zhongchi and Hu Yizang

Equally commendable as this artistic sensibility are the Japanese people's politeness and human touch. We experienced this at the inn in Kobe. We were Chinese and new to such inns, but we did not feel the trouble of being strangers in a strange land. The innkeeper was very attentive and polite, and the waitresses who served us were also very endearing. Although they were poor farm girls, they had none of the rude manners. They were both generous and clever. They spoke to us with the utmost respect. At first, she brought tea sets and a fruit box filled with Kobe's specialty, "tile crackers," and knelt beside us to pour tea respectfully. Later, at mealtime, she knelt down to serve us rice, putting the rice bowl on a wooden tray and handing it to us as if offering a sacrifice. When entering and leaving the door, she always bowed. At night, she made up the cotton quilt for us, asked if there was anything else we needed, and then said good night and walked out.

The waitresses in the inns belong to the oppressed class of Japan. Their respectful politeness can also be said to be due to their profession. However, the fundamental reason is still in the traditional moral habits of Japan. People of all classes in Japan, whether men or women, have always been particular about politeness. Bows are always forty degrees. There are also many honorifics in the language. This humble politeness, which represents the inherent morality of Japan, along with the inherent art of Japan, was praised by Lafcadio Hearn (a deceased British writer who lived in Japan for a long time) with the highest adjectives. In today's era, these two are still worthy of our praise. These two symbolize the spirit of ancient Japan, that is, the spirit of peaceful Japan; only with this spirit can the feelings of China and Japan be reconciled.

But unfortunately, this lovely spirit of ancient Japan has begun to waver. Because since Western, especially German, civilization was introduced to Japan, a new spirit has gradually swelled up to eliminate that lovely traditional spirit. Our life in the Kobe inn made us feel that way in practice. We were sitting cross-legged on the mats, admiring the simple beauty of the purely Japanese-style interior decoration, as well as the polite and gentle demeanor of the maid who served us, and enjoying the leisurely and peaceful taste expressed by the inscription on the plaque, when suddenly a rumbling giant feast came over, shaking the entire house we were living in, and all the windows rattled. Then we shattered the previous daydream and realized that we were in a noisy international city. We looked out the window and saw a rapidly running train passing over the elevated railway opposite us. The Kobe elevated railway has not been completed for long. The rails are laid on steel and cement viaducts that are two meters high, with evenly arranged piers, in the middle of which buildings can be built or roads can be opened. Now this elevated railway has directly connected to Osaka. It only takes twenty-eight minutes to get there by taking the limited express train from Sannomiya Station in Kobe.

Huge and amazing construction projects such as elevated railways and subways have been developing very rapidly in Japan in recent years. This is not necessarily due to the needs of industrial development. The fundamental reason is first in the competitive psychology of Japanese imperialists. They not only want to compete with other powerful countries in armaments. Even in urban construction, when they see what amazing constructions are in the big cities such as New York and London, they have to follow suit, no matter how heavy the burden on their own people. The second is that in recent years, the tide of the world economic panic has left the capital of Japan's major financial groups with no proper outlet. They have to use huge public construction projects to absorb excess capital, excess labor, and excess industrial materials.

The material civilization of Japan, from the surface of the city, has indeed reached a very high level. However, the general public can only firmly maintain an extremely simple traditional life in terms of clothing, food, and housing. In the inn in Kobe, we also enjoyed that kind of life.

We took a bath in the inn's bathroom in the Japanese way, changed into a set of kimonos specially prepared by the inn, and returned to our room, which was covered with twelve mats and had a small table and a charcoal brazier in the middle. After resting for a while, the maid brought in dinner. So we each ate from a lacquered tray with four short legs. The lacquer tray contained various kinds of bowls and plates, filled with raw fish, grilled fish, fish soup, and two slices of yellow radish and a small handful of half-cooked green vegetables. These Japanese dishes were all cooked very simply, and they were not very palatable to us, who were used to greasy Chinese dishes. The dark red raw fish is considered a Japanese delicacy, but we disliked the fishy smell, so we poured boiling water on it and ate it, and then we felt a little taste.

Kobe Streetscape

Joint Transportation of the Jiangnan-Nanjing-Shanghai Railways and China Merchants Steam Navigation Company 60

A decision has been made to begin a six-month trial operation on the 21st. After the expiration of the period, further negotiations will be held to continue the operation. Ceremony to Move the Coffin of Hu Hanmin to the Cemetery; No Fewer Than Ten Thousand People Participated in Holding the Ropes; Government Offices and Businesses Lowered Flags to Half-Mast; Humen Fort Fired Salutes to Express Grief; The Cemetery is Grand and Magnificent 63

Guangzhou Correspondence: After Hu Hanmin's death, his coffin was kept in the Sun Yat-sen Memorial Hall for a long time. It was not until the 13th of this month that the ceremony to move the coffin was held, and the ceremony was extremely grand. The funeral committee had previously selected a burial site at Shiling Ridge in Douwenlong, Longyandong, in the northeastern suburbs, with an area of ​​more than a thousand mu. In addition to building the tomb, a mausoleum was built around it, with a grand scale. Next to Shiling is the Guangzeng Highway (from Guangzhou to Zengcheng County). The funeral committee specially opened a branch road on the Guangzeng Highway to directly reach the Shiling cemetery, which is convenient for transportation. The hearse for transporting the coffin was specially purchased from abroad, about thirteen feet long and seven feet wide. Rails are laid inside the car for moving the coffin up and down. The four sides of the car are decorated with black glass windows and doors. White cloths and white silk balls are attached to the car door. There are also water-patterned white silk ribbons around both sides of the car. The outer railing of the car is decorated with blue satin, which is extremely simple. Hu's portrait is also specially made, more than ten feet high and six feet wide, with Hu's portrait hanging inside. There are sixteen porters in front and behind the bier.

At six o'clock in the morning on the 13th, representatives from various provinces and cities who were holding the ropes arrived one after another. People from military, political, and party circles also participated. They included Chen Jitang, Li Zongren, Lin Yunkai, Lin Yizhong, Xiao Focheng, Xie Yingzhou, Ou Fangpu, He Qinong, Chen Zhongfu, Liao Yuzan, Gan Jiehou, Li Xiangen, Li Luchao, Huang Jilu, Wang Xiaowen, Liu Jiwen, Li Xiaosheng, Huang Xuchu, members of the Southwest Political Affairs Council, Guangdong Provincial Government, Provincial and Municipal Party Headquarters, various committees, and representatives from various groups, totaling more than a thousand people. The presidium elected Li Zongren as the master of ceremonies, and the master of ceremonies announced the order of the departure ceremony: (1) Stand at attention, (2) Play mourning music, (3) Present flowers, presented by the master of ceremonies Li himself, (4) Read the eulogy, (5) Silent mourning, (6) Bow three times, (7) Play mourning music, (8) Start the departure. The rope holders lined up in order, led by the bandmaster Deng Gang with a silver band, followed by the portrait pavilion, hearse, and then the Hu family's car, with the military police at the rear. At 8:20 am, the departure began. The Humen Fortress fired nineteen salutes, and all government offices and shops in the city lowered their flags to half-mast to express grief. At the time of departure, the procession followed Jixiang Road and exited the city through Huiai East Road. The order of the procession was as follows: First Row: (1) Cavalry officer riding a black horse holding a flag to lead the way, (2) Two flag-guarding cavalrymen, each riding a black horse and carrying a long gun, (3) Two flag-holding cavalrymen, riding black horses, holding the party and national flags on the left and right, (4) Two flag-guarding cavalrymen, (5) First Group Army band, (6) A company of cavalry, all holding lances. Second Row: (1) Guangdong Military and Political School band, (2) A regiment of infantry. Third Row: (1) Fleet band, (2) Marine Corps, (3) Naval soldiers, (4) Air Force escort team. Fourth Row: (1) Provincial Public Security Bureau silver band, (2) Police team, (3) Police security team. Fifth Row: (1) Xiangqin University silver band, (2) Representatives of agricultural, industrial, commercial, academic, women's, overseas Chinese, and freelance professional groups, (3) Foreign guests, (4) Chiefs and staff of local party, government, and military agencies, staff of the National Funeral Ceremony Office, (5) Representatives of party, government, military, and other groups from various provinces, cities, and special regions, (6) A squad of military police. Seventh Row: (1) Municipal Government silver band, (2) Portrait pavilion, (3) Hearse, (4) Family car, (5) A squad of military police. Eighth Row: A company of cavalry, holding lances at the rear. The above eight rows, with a total of more than ten thousand rope holders, each with black gauze wrapped around their arms, walked in an orderly and solemn manner along the way. Because of the large number of people, it took three hours for the entire team to leave the city and proceed to Dongsha Road in the suburbs. At 9:30 am, the first row arrived at Huanghuagang. A farewell place had been prepared there in advance. Officials from various agencies, representatives from various groups, and students from various schools all held a farewell ceremony there. Therefore, as soon as they arrived, they lined up on both sides, waiting quietly for the coffin to pass by and paying their respects. Not long after, the hearse passed in front of them. The farewell participants stood on the roadside, soldiers and police stood at attention, officers saluted, and officials and representatives of groups took off their hats to salute. At 11:50 am, after the hearse passed by, the rope holders from all walks of life dispersed. The officials and foreign guests who escorted the coffin to the cemetery then switched to cars. At about 12 noon, they arrived at the cemetery. A giant hall was built in front of the tomb, covering an area of ​​300 mu. The hall was divided into two parts, front and back. The front part was the hall, which displayed Hu's life supplies, such as chairs, tables, stationery, vases, and desks. Hu's "Bu Kui Shi Poems" and various posthumous works and manuscripts were displayed on the desk. The back part of the hall was used by Hu's family to guard the spirit and rest. There were also guest lounges, reception rooms, and guard rooms on the left and right sides of the tomb. At 1:00 pm, the officials who sent the coffin had arrived and rested briefly. At 2:50 pm, the coffin was transported in. The coffin senders lined up on the roadside again. As the hearse passed by, mourning music was played. Everyone walked to the burial site on Lion Mountain to send the coffin. At 3:00 pm, they arrived. At 4:00 pm, more than a thousand people who attended the funeral respectfully paid their respects. Lin Yunkai presided over the ceremony. The ceremony was completed, and it was already past 5:00 pm. They then dispersed and returned to Guangzhou.

Taiwan Restricts the Entry of Chinese Laborers; Chinese Laborers Came to Taiwan Originally Recruited by the Japanese; Concerned About the Excess, They Added Restrictions 64

Xiamen Correspondence: In recent years, due to the decline of industry and commerce and frequent disasters in Fujian Province, many people have lost their jobs. Laborers have flocked to foreign countries to make a living. Taiwan happened to increase the production of military, industrial raw materials, and minerals, and needed labor. Therefore, they came to Fujian to recruit laborers from Putian, Fuqing, and Wenzhou in Zhejiang to go to Taiwan. According to Taiwan news, according to the statistics of the Taiwan Governor's Office, more than 7,000 Chinese laborers came to Taiwan from January to the end of June this year. These Chinese laborers are more able to endure hardship than Japanese and Taiwanese, and their wages are also lower. Therefore, many mines, factories, and shops are happy to use them. As a result, Taiwanese laborers have been greatly affected. The number of unemployed workers has recently increased to 10,000. If this continues, the number of unemployed will inevitably increase. The Taiwan Governor's Office then ordered the Foreign Affairs Section and the Security Section to coordinate countermeasures. As a result, it was decided to restrict the entry of Chinese laborers and immediately ordered the Nanguo Company, which specializes in handling the procedures for Chinese laborers to go to Taiwan, to do so. Taiwan recruits Chinese laborers when they need them, fearing that they will not come. When they feel they have too many, they refuse them, fearing that they will not be able to get rid of them. (July 16th)

Solar Eclipse 77

— Central Broadcasting · Lecture Manuscript Yu Qingsong

Esteemed listeners, the most significant astronomical phenomenon this year, capable of mobilizing astronomers, physicists, and meteorologists worldwide, is the total solar eclipse on June 19th. In the history of Chinese astronomy, this eclipse is particularly memorable because it marks the first time China sent representatives to observe a solar eclipse alongside renowned international astronomers. I am fortunate to be one of those participants, so today I will briefly share the observation process and the general significance of observing a solar eclipse with you all.

We know that solar and lunar eclipses are merely celestial phenomena resulting from the alignment of the Earth, Sun, and Moon. When the Moon passes between the Earth and the Sun, it blocks a portion of the sunlight from reaching the Earth, causing a solar eclipse. Therefore, a solar eclipse always occurs during the new moon (the first day of the lunar month). When the Moon's umbral cone falls on a particular location, a total solar eclipse occurs, where the Sun is completely obscured. While solar eclipses always happen during new moons, not every new moon results in a solar eclipse. This is due to the relative positions of the Earth and Moon's orbits. As for the frequency of solar eclipses, statistical results show that there are 8,000 occurrences in 3,368 years, averaging 237 solar eclipses per century. Among these, 66 are total eclipses. This is for the entire Earth. Assuming China occupies two percent of the Earth's surface, the probability of a total eclipse's center falling within China is, on average, once per century. Examining this more closely, we know that from 1542 (the 21st year of the Ming Dynasty's Jiajing era) to the present, nearly 400 years, there have been a total of 26 total solar eclipses passing over China. From this year onward, there will be 10 total solar eclipses visible in China within a century. However, only four of these will occur around midday in the past four centuries, and only one in the next century. Further specifying that it crosses the densely populated areas around the Yellow River and Yangtze River, and is visible in the central region of the mainland near midday, there have only been two such occurrences in 500 years. One was on August 11, 1542 (the 7th lunar month of the 21st year of the Ming Dynasty's Jiajing era, Ji-You day) at noon, with the eclipse over the Yellow River basin. The other was on September 21, 1941 (the 30th year of the Republic of China) at noon, with the eclipse over the Yangtze River basin. These two total eclipses are almost exactly 400 years apart, making such an opportunity incredibly rare.

What exactly happens during a total solar eclipse? Based on what I witnessed this time in Hokkaido, Japan, as the Sun is gradually obscured by the Moon, sunlight gradually diminishes. When the Sun is almost entirely hidden, a particularly bright light appears at its edge, resembling a diamond ring. Instantly, this brilliant section vanishes, and an extremely bright halo appears around the Sun, known as the corona. This corona's appearance varies each time. This time, the corona was pentagonal in shape, its length nearly the same as the Sun's diameter. Simultaneously, between the dark Sun's edge and the corona, there were five solar prominences, red flames. Three were scattered individually, and two were clustered together. Near the Sun, a very bright star, Venus, was also visible. These phenomena lasted for one minute and fifty-odd seconds, then completely disappeared, and sunlight gradually brightened again. During totality, the overall brightness was similar to that of a full moon. However, the light during a full moon is white, while the light during totality is yellowish-green, making it seem darker. Shortly before totality, many crows were seen flying back to their nests, and about twenty minutes after totality, we heard roosters crowing, as they mistook the event for dawn.

The duration of totality is at most seven minutes. This time I saw one minute and fifty-odd seconds. About six years ago, the total eclipse seen near San Francisco, USA, lasted only one and a half seconds. As for the total eclipse visible in China on September 21, 1941 (the 30th year of the Republic of China), it could last up to three minutes and twenty seconds in one location. For such a short period of time, astronomers, physicists, and meteorologists worldwide spend hundreds of thousands of dollars and endure arduous journeys to observe and study these phenomena. For example, for this solar eclipse, most European astronomers gathered in western Soviet Union. In Hokkaido, Japan, virtually all Japanese astronomers, physicists, and meteorologists, regardless of age, participated, forming thirty-eight teams totaling one hundred and seventy people. The government increased the budget by hundreds of thousands of yen. Besides Chinese teams, there were also observation teams from Britain, the United States, Poland, Czechoslovakia, India, and so on. Why spend so much money and involve scholars worldwide for such a short period? It is because observing this phenomenon provides many opportunities for scientific research. I will now discuss the most important of these:

(1) Determining the relative positions of the Sun and Moon.

(2) Capturing images of the sky near the Sun to determine the existence of planets within Mercury's orbit and observing the bending of starlight passing near the Sun's edge, providing data for the study of general relativity.

(3) Taking photographs of the corona and prominences to study their changes.

(4) Conducting spectroscopic observations of the inversion layer, photosphere, and corona.

(5) Measuring the light intensity of the corona.

(6) Measuring the radiant heat of the corona.

(7) Measuring the polarization of light from the corona.

(8) Observing changes in various meteorological elements, magnetic influences, radio wave effects, and so on as the eclipse intensifies.

In short, observing solar eclipses can not only solve astronomical problems but also contribute to research in physics and meteorology. Because of its significant scientific value, each time there is a total solar eclipse, governments spend hundreds of thousands of dollars or dispatch warships to escort observation teams to their destinations for observation. However, if it rains, all efforts are in vain. For example, among the observation teams in Hokkaido this time, the British team had the most and largest equipment. The observation personnel arrived at the destination from Britain in early May and spent over a month preparing. Unfortunately, due to clouds during the eclipse, they could not observe it. The Chinese observation team dispatched to Boli (Khabarovsk) in the Soviet Union also encountered the same misfortune.

The goals of China's dispatch of an observation team this time were roughly threefold. First, to capture images of the corona to study its light intensity changes. As a result, three satisfactory photographs of the corona were taken. Second, to gather reference data for the solar eclipse visible in China on September 21, 1941 (the 30th year of the Republic of China). Much experience was gained. Third, to enhance the general public's knowledge, so three sets of films were taken, which will be publicly screened in the future.

Photograph of the corona taken on June 19th during totality, with an exposure time of five seconds.

The central black circle is the Sun, the surrounding white light is the corona, and the white spots on the black edge are the white prominences.

Above is the welcome gate erected by Giko Village in Hokkaido, Japan, specifically to welcome the Chinese observation team. Below are members of the Chinese observation team.

Nanyang Commercial Inspection Group Set Sail Yesterday Morning on Dutch Vessel · Enthusiastic Farewell from All Sectors · Returning to Country After Three-Month Inspection · Carrying Over One Hundred Boxes of Domestic Products in Preparation for Exhibition 78

The Nanyang Commercial Inspection Group organized by the China National Industries Overseas Trade Association, a party of fifteen led by the head and deputy heads Gao Shiheng and Hu Shicheng, set sail yesterday morning at half past ten o'clock on the Java Mailboat Company's Zhini Geila Wheel. More than a hundred representatives from all walks of life went to see them off. The details are recorded as follows:

The group included head Gao Shiheng, deputy head Hu Shicheng, chief secretary Zhang Zuyin, Shanghai accountant Zhuang Maoru, public relations Xu Xuejie, secretary Yang Chonggao, and members Li Shenyan, Lu Zixian, Deng Qiyao, Xu Zhaolin, Jiang Junrui, Gao Juxin, Zhou Guojun, Wang Gongquan, Zhu Qizu, and others, fifteen in total. All wore white drill suits, gray pith helmets, black ties, and black leather shoes, appearing neat and spirited. The vessel weighed anchor at half past ten in the morning.

Those who went to see them off included representatives from the Machine-Made National Products Factories Joint Association, the Shanghai National Products Movement Joint Association, the National Products Production and Sales Association, the China National Industries Overseas Trade Association, as well as representatives from the Meyer Silk Weaving Factory, Huachang Enamelware Factory, Washeng Electric Appliance Factory, Home Industry Cooperative, Xingye Ceramic Tile Company, Yongzhou Paint Company, and others, including Hu Xiyuan, Cai Shengbai, Zhang Huikang, Huang Renzhi, Xu Xiaochu, Wang Xingyao, Cheng Shouchung, Xiang Kangyuan, Ye Youcai, and relatives and friends of the group members, totaling over a hundred people, creating a very enthusiastic scene.

Inaugural Meeting of the Forensic Medicine Review Board 84

The Ministry of Judicial Administration, in order to plan the improvement of forensic medicine and assist in solving difficult forensic medical problems, has specially established a Forensic Medicine Review Board, hiring domestic medical experts to serve in groups. The inaugural meeting was held on the 11th of this month at the Bankers' Association in this city. Minister Wang was unable to attend due to attending the Second Plenary Session, so he specially dispatched Zheng Yue, Chief Prosecutor of the Jiangsu High Court Second Branch, and Zhao Shibei, Chief Prosecutor of the High Court Third Branch, to deliver congratulatory speeches on his behalf. The details of the meeting are recorded below.

Attendees

Those present: Zeng Guangfang, Zhao Chengxia, Kuang Ankun, Liang Hanfen, Le Wenzhao, Weng Zhilong, Liu Yongchun, Cheng Muyi, Chen Hongkang, Zhu Hengbi, Niu Huisheng (representing Sun), Shen Chengwu, Guo Qiyuan, Pan Chenggao, Yan Fuching, Li Qingmao, Fu Wenshou, Sun Dafang, Zheng Yue and Zhao Shibei representing the Ministry of Judicial Administration, Chairman Sun Kuifang, recorders Chen Renjun and Zu Zhaoji.

Meeting Proceedings

The meeting was opened as scheduled. The chairman delivered an opening speech, stating in essence: "Today is the day of the establishment of the Forensic Medicine Review Board of the Ministry of Judicial Administration. I should use simple language to announce the purpose of the meeting. As civilization advances, the methods of committing crimes become more complex, and the scope of forensic medicine also expands accordingly. Today, the identification of cases in forensic medicine requires the knowledge of all scientific medicine. Therefore, solving all cases with all knowledge cannot be achieved by the knowledge of one or two people alone. It is necessary to gather the specialized knowledge of many people in order to cope with everything. The establishment of this association adheres to the above purpose, to work together and jointly promote the development of the association. The future forensic medicine is deeply relied upon," and incidentally reported that at the last standing committee meeting, the正副主任s of each group were elected, and the procedural rules were drafted. At this meeting, it is planned to discuss the procedural rules.

Minister's Congratulatory Speech

Next, a congratulatory speech was delivered by a representative of Minister Wang of the Ministry of Judicial Administration, stating in part that today is the day of the establishment of the Forensic Medicine Review Board. Medical experts from all over the country are gathered here. Because of the meeting of the Second Plenary Session of the Central Committee, this Minister has not been able to attend the ceremony in person. I hereby express my feelings and express infinite hope, and wish the review board success. The intention of the Ministry to establish this association is to promote the development of forensic medicine and the editing of forensic medical textbooks. In terms of the former, forensic examinations of cases are to discover the truth and achieve credible verdicts, which is of the deepest help to the trial affairs. Forensic medicine in our country is not yet developed. Although a Forensic Medicine Research Institute has been established to specialize in this matter, given the size of our country and the number of criminal cases, difficult problems arise from time to time, and the discussions are inconsistent and the clues are extremely complex. It is not easy to find a proper solution without relying on the strength of the masses and the strategies of the masses. Each expert's suggestions, as well as the matters submitted by the Ministry for discussion by the Forensic Medicine Research Institute, will certainly be able to make refined contributions based on their superior academic experience, so that the sentence will be in line with the crime and the crime will be in line with the circumstances. This is one. In terms of the latter, the lack of forensic medical personnel and equipment in our country is extremely serious. The implementation of鑑定检驗s in various courts still mostly embraces the old and outdated, which is not in line with the theory. During this period of transition from the old to the new, it is urgent to create 檢驗人村. Moreover, the compilation of standard 检验 books to unify the national 檢政 and teaching materials should not be delayed. These standard teaching materials should refer to the new law and improve the existing rules, so as to be suitable for practical application. It is hoped that the training of 檢驗 personnel can be regarded as the standard. Each expert in this field will certainly be able to express their great opinions and integrate them into great achievements, so that forensic medical education will be popularized as soon as possible. This is two. The above two points are only the main points that the Ministry considers urgent. All the gentlemen are famous scholars and medical scholars, and their enthusiastic support or instructions to this association will be a hundred times more than this. This Minister, on behalf of the national forensic medical community, extends the most sincere welcome and gratitude," and the second one said that at today's inaugural meeting of the Forensic Medicine Review Board, Chief Zheng and this Chief were ordered to represent Minister Wang of the Ministry of Judicial Administration to deliver congratulatory speeches and host a banquet. In addition to the Minister's congratulatory speech, which has been delivered by Chief Zheng, this Chief further extended Minister Wang's meaning, and briefly stated one or two of the important points in which this association is related to judicial inspection, in order to extend congratulations. In the past, the inspection in our country was based solely on the "Collected Cases of Injustice Rectified," but as times have changed and science has progressed, the methods of injury and death are beyond the scope of the "Collected Cases of Injustice Rectified," and the "Collected Cases of Injustice Rectified" has become an outdated academic subject. After the founding of the Republic of China, the Ministry of Justice of Beijing once issued a book entitled "New Knowledge of Inspection," which was not detailed and was not the result of discussions among forensic medical experts from all over the country. Moreover, because it has not been unified for many years, some provinces have followed it and some have not, and it still cannot adapt to the times. This is why the Ministry of Judicial Administration first established a Forensic Medicine Research Institute, with the aim of creating forensic medical personnel who can meet the requirements of the times. Now that this association has been established, it has gathered specialist scholars together, and there is no difficulty in solving all the difficult problems in the 检验 field. In the future, the forensic doctors who conduct inspections in various courts, as well as the prosecutors who go to the site for the 相驗, and the judges who judge the cases, will be able to take the deliberations of the Muhui as the standard, so as not to be at a loss, and the parties will have nothing to use to argue, and the sentence will be free of errors and the court will be free of injustice. The judicial world should release a different color, which can be celebrated for the future of justice, and so on.

Public Concession Factory Workers: Over 3,400 Factories, Totaling Over 170,000 People 85

According to the Guomin News Agency, a recent industrial survey of the Public Concession found a total of 3,421 factories of all sizes. The distribution of these factories is as follows: the Eastern District has the most, with 2,050 factories, accounting for 60%. Among these, 1,163 are located west of Dalian Wan Road, accounting for about half of the district and more than one-third of the Public Concession. Next is the Northern District, with 589 factories, accounting for 17% of the total. However, these factories are smaller in scale. The Western District follows, with 565 factories, accounting for about 16% of the total. The total number of workers is 170,704. The distribution of workers also shows the Eastern District in the leading position, with 86,724 workers, accounting for over 50% of the total. Within this district, the area east of Dalian Wan Road has the most workers, with 52,552. The Western District follows, with 46,158 workers, accounting for over 27%. Furthermore, among the various industries in the Public Concession, the machinery and metal manufacturing industry has the largest number of factories, with 1,108 factories, accounting for one-third of the total. The printing industry follows, with 663 factories, accounting for 20% of the total. The textile industry is next, with 567 factories, accounting for 16% of the total. In terms of the number of workers, the textile industry has the largest number, with 75,242 workers, accounting for over 44% of the total. The food and beverage industry follows, with 25,886 workers, accounting for over 15% of the total. The machinery and metal manufacturing industry is next, with 19,051 workers, accounting for over 11% of the total.

Tea Exports Increase Sharply 90

According to the Xin Xin News Agency, since the National Economic Council established tea planting experiment stations in the tea-producing areas of Anhui and Jiangxi provinces two years ago, researching and improving planting and scientific processing methods, and providing practical guidance to tea farmers, urging improvements and strictly prohibiting tea merchants from adulterating inferior tea, the quality has gradually gained the trust of foreign tea merchants. This year, Anhui and Jiangxi provinces have also implemented unified control over transportation and sales, which has been convenient for foreign merchants. Therefore, since the new tea season, tea merchants from various countries such as England, France, and Russia in Shanghai have been eagerly purchasing tea. Various types of red and green tea arriving in Shanghai are in high demand, and prices are gradually rising. In recent days, the selling price of high-grade tea has exceeded 80 yuan per box, and the market situation is the best in recent years. Moreover, since January, merchant ships heading to France, England, and Russia have been loaded with large quantities of tea. The quantity transported to Russia has increased by about 30-40% compared to last year. In the past two days, 280 tons were shipped to England, and over 2,500 boxes were shipped to France. Large quantities are still stored in warehouses, waiting to be loaded onto ships. However, foreign merchants are purchasing only high-quality tea, and inferior tea is ignored. According to inspections by European tea merchants, if the work of improving Chinese tea can continue unremittingly, it will surely surpass Ceylon, India, and Java tea, and restore the inherent reputation of Chinese tea overseas.

China Merchants Steam Navigation Company Reports No Responsibility for Damaging Tugboat 91

When the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's "Huaxin" ship was loading cargo in Haizhou, the Shanghai-based Jardine Matheson sent the large tugboat "Saint Cypress" to Haizhou to rescue the "Chunhe" ship, and it was also docked in the port. The tugboat had eight steel plates damaged by the "Huaxin" ship. According to Mr. Tang Danhua, director of the China United Ship Insurance Association, the owner of the "Huaxin" ship officially reported that he arrived in Shanghai yesterday and stated that when the "Huaxin" ship was tightly docked at the Haizhou pier, the stern cable platform was excessively impacted by the turbulent currents, causing the cable platform to suddenly break. The stern lost its mooring force, and the ship was pushed outwards by the current, causing it to collide with and damage the Jardine Matheson "Saint Cypress" tugboat. This was due to the pier breaking and the turbulent currents, which could not be resisted by human force, and therefore, the ship insurance does not bear any responsibility.
