Freedom vs. Control in Trade Union Membership: An Opinion 93

Labor expert Mr. Chen Zhenlu expressed his views, saying that in various countries, workers' organizations initially had no freedom to form trade unions. After gaining freedom, they were initially restricted by the government, and later their own freedom devolved into laissez-faire, resulting in the inertia of freedom. As a result, the liberal organization of trade unions had to change course. After the European War, the freedom of trade union organizations fully manifested its irregularity, lack of unity, inertia and dispersion, laissez-faire and incompetence. Therefore, the former liberal organizations have mostly been replaced by controlled organizations. For example, in Soviet Russia, organizations must be within the party line; in Italy and Germany, trade union actions must be in line with the national will; and in France and the United States, importance is attached to negotiations with workers' organizations.

Speaking of freedom, it is initially unobjectionable, but when freedom leads to abuses, it must be remedied. As Roosevelt said, "I believe that the interpretation of freedom should be that we can provide more freedom and security to the general public than before." This is indeed a sharp rebuke to the freedom claimed by American capitalists. Paul Pic said, "The principle of freedom should be placed before the interests of society," which is the same idea. Because traditional freedom has become the freedom of a minority of capitalists, depriving the majority of those who participate in actual production of freedom. Freedom has been too much influenced by individualism, disregarding the general interests of society. This kind of freedom is like what Proudhon said, "Private property is theft" (Sa Propriete cestbvol) (Note 1). Only its drawbacks are seen, and its benefits are not seen, so it should naturally be corrected. The extreme of freedom will lead to laissez-faire, dispersion, and disorganization, like anarchy. Economic liberalism is therefore regarded as a state of anarchy in production. The extreme of freedom also fully cultivates social inertia. Individuals pursue only their own interests, ignorant of social interests, and rely on the inferior nature of isolation to live in comfort, lacking a sense of community, and willingly defying public opinion to perish. This kind of individualistic freedom is a freedom that leads to a dead end. If it is replaced by collective freedom, it is a freedom that leads to a broad path. The two should be distinguished, and the dead end should not be mistaken for the broad path.

Recently, the Shanghai Federation of Trade Unions submitted a request to the central government to amend Article 20 of the Trade Union Law, which states that "Trade unions shall not force workers to join or prevent them from withdrawing," and Article 21, "Trade union members may withdraw from the union at any time," to read, "All workers in the same industry or unified occupation organized by a trade union shall join the respective trade union as members," and "Trade union members shall not arbitrarily withdraw from the trade union or fail to pay membership dues without a legitimate reason approved by the union." This can be said to be transforming the trade union organization from laissez-faire to control, from freedom that is off track to freedom that is restricted on the track. In other words, it is to correct the loose inertia and incompetence of the trade union organization, making it a disciplined and mobilized group. Whether explained from the perspective of principles or from the perspective of the actual needs of extraordinary times, it can be considered an appropriate suggestion. Unfortunately, this suggestion has not yet been adopted by the central government. According to Executive Yuan Instruction No. 713, after the Ministry of Industry deliberated and replied, "Article 20, Paragraph 1 and Article 21 of the Trade Union Law are intended to prevent trade unions from hindering the freedom of workers, and there is no need for amendment." This kind of reasoning is not without room for discussion.

The so-called "individual freedom of workers" should be "the freedom for individual workers to obtain security," as Roosevelt said, freedom should be more freedom and security for the general public than before. It should also be as Bic said, "The principle of freedom should be respected, but this principle should be placed before the interests of society." Because the result of individual freedom has two aspects, good and evil. The good aspect is its bright side, which improves the status of workers. The evil aspect is its dark side, which makes workers' lives sink deeper into the abyss. Since the country has labor legislation, its intention is originally to protect workers. Therefore, it is necessary to distinguish between the two results of individual freedom for workers. The good results can protect workers and should be retained. The evil results often isolate workers and allow them to be defeated one by one by capital groups. Each claims to be for the freedom of trade unions, but it is actually suicide for workers and should be eliminated in order to conform to the basic intent of national legislation to protect workers.

The era of opposing social interests based on the reason of individual freedom has passed. In the past, national legislation to protect child labor and female labor was often opposed by citing the principle of individual freedom. However, national legislation to protect child labor and female labor was eventually implemented. At the beginning of the establishment of the collective bargaining law, it was opposed by employers, and the reason was also based on the freedom of individual contracts. However, to this day, more and more workers are signing contracts with employers in the name of trade unions, and the constitutional characteristics of collective agreements are becoming more and more effective. In general, individual freedom initially has its virtue, but later it changes its nature (Note 2). Since the drawbacks have occurred, they must be corrected. Therefore, today, the value of individual freedom lies only in the good aspects of freedom, only in the aspects of freedom that are consistent with social benefits, and only in the aspects of freedom that conform to the intent of protecting the interests of labor.

Based on this, the "individual freedom of workers" in the legislative intent of Article 20, Paragraph 1 and Article 21 of the Trade Union Law should not fall into the stereotype of the traditional individualistic interpretation of freedom. Instead, the actual meaning of freedom should be adopted as a social, majority, and labor security interpretation. Therefore, if the amendment of Article 20, Paragraph 1 and Article 21 of the Trade Union Law can increase the centripetal force of workers towards trade unions and improve the collective interests of workers, then amending it into a more rigorous and controlled trade union organization is the beginning of implementing the legislative protection of labor and striving for progress day by day, and should not be rigidly rejected without consideration.

During the European War, trade unions in France, England, Germany were inspired by nationalism, helping the government to resist the enemy and mobilizing without hindrance. This is because trade unions can have the effect of using workers as if they were appendages, like using fingers. In this extraordinary period in China, the mobilization, training, and preparation of workers belonging to trade unions are extremely important. Without a rigorous organization and the role of control, it will be impossible to achieve the effect of unified will, orderly steps, and decisive command. If the mobilization order is issued but cannot be mobilized, then having an organization is like having no organization. The result of blind and disorderly actions will inevitably have an unimaginable impact on the overall situation of resisting aggression and saving the nation. This should be planned for early on. Then, changing the peacetime wording of Article 20, Paragraph 1 and Article 21 of the Trade Union Law to extraordinary period wording is even more urgently felt in reality. Now that the Shanghai Federation of Trade Unions has requested the central government to reconsider, it is hoped that the administrative authorities and legislative figures will examine the past of worker organizations, pay attention to the trends and needs of the times, and discuss in detail the legislative intent of each article of the Trade Union Law, the "freedom of individual workers," and think towards its bright side, so that Chinese trade union organizations can gain greater centripetal force, transforming freedom with drawbacks into freedom without drawbacks, correcting individual laissez-faire into collective control, and progressing from relaxed inertia to a tense and capable spirit.

Note 1: Proudhon said: "Private property is both justice and theft" (Saproiteest unematitution de jusitce et la propricete cest levol). Therefore, private property, from one perspective, may be fair, but when its drawbacks lead to unearned gain, it evolves into the ugly drama of theft. This is another aspect of the result. Freedom is also like this. Although it may be valuable at first, as Madame Roland said, "Oh Freedom, Freedom, many crimes are committed in your name." From another perspective, the impact of its drawbacks is also unimaginable.

Note 2: This is actually indicated by the physical principle of "quantitative change leading to qualitative change." The moderate amount of individual freedom has inherent virtue, but the excessive amount of individual freedom has evil nature.

Chongqing Tung Oil Firms Join Improvement Plan; Representative Yang Dianzhang Already Arrived in Shanghai from Hankou 94

The Chinese Vegetable Oil Plant, initiated and organized by the Ministry of Industry, aims to improve the production and sales of the tung oil industry nationwide. Since the establishment of the preparatory office, inland oil merchants, aware of their own needs, have followed suit, either inquiring by letter or telegram or sending personnel to Shanghai to negotiate. For example, the representatives of the Wanxian Oil and Grain Industry and Import Industry came to Shanghai some time ago to negotiate successfully, as previously reported. Chongqing is the second largest tung oil market in Sichuan, with annual exports of about 150,000 dan. The operators are divided into oil firms and foreign firms. There are two foreign firms in the city, and the original number of oil firms was five or six. In the past year or two, oil prices have risen repeatedly, gradually increasing to twelve. Now, the oil firms are afraid that there will be too many operators, leading to unfair competition. In order to rectify the oil industry, they have initiated the organization of the Chongqing Tung Oil Firms Guild, restricting the number of firms. It has been approved by the Chongqing Municipal Government for record. Because the vegetable oil plant is about to be established, the guild has specially sent representative Yang Dianzhang to Shanghai to negotiate. Mr. Yang flew from Hankou to Shanghai on the 15th. It is reported that he will soon discuss the conditions with Mr. Zhang Jiazhu, director of the oil plant's preparatory office.

Gold Trading Declines Sharply; Handling Fees Increased 95

In view of the sharp decline in trading, the Gold Exchange, in order to maintain business, decided through a board meeting to increase the collection of handling fees from July 16. After consultation with its brokers' association, it was approved to be implemented from the 20th. The details are as follows:

Maintaining Business by Increasing Handling Fees

Previously, the daily gold trading volume of the Gold Exchange was always above 100,000 units, but now it has sharply declined to only 20,000 to 30,000 units. The original handling fee was 2.5 li per unit. After deducting the 25% broker incentive, the exchange actually received 1.575 li. Now, the board of directors has decided that, in order to maintain business, the handling fee will be increased to 1 jiao per unit, including the previous fee, from July 16. Its Announcement No. 2176 states: "Now, the board of directors has decided to temporarily change the handling fee paid by brokers to the exchange to 1 jiao in national currency per unit of gold trading, excluding the 2.5 fen in national currency broker incentive. The exchange will actually receive 7.5 fen in national currency for the handling fee. It will be implemented from the 16th of this month. This announcement is made to notify all brokers, in addition to a letter to the Brokers' Association."

Market Guild Postpones Implementation

Mr. Zhan Liansheng, chairman of the Brokers' Association, convened a meeting of all brokers regarding the handling fee increase. The brokers requested a reduction and negotiated with Mr. Xu Longzhu, chairman of the Gold Exchange. Now, an agreement has been reached to follow the board's decision, but the implementation is postponed to the 20th. Announcement No. 2178 of the Market Guild states: "Now, approval is given for the request by the chairman of the Brokers' Association to change the commission and handling fees because the time is too short, and it is feared that the clients are not yet aware of it. It is proposed to postpone it for three days. After investigation, the requested matters are factual and should be postponed for three days. The changed method will be collected from the 20th of this month (Monday). This is hereby announced."

Extending the Shanghai-Wusong Branch Line; Two Railway Bureaus Send Personnel to Survey the Roadbed; Construction Will Commence After Approval by the Ministry 96

According to the Dagong News Agency, the Baoshan Shanghai Fellow-Villagers Association stated that the Shanghai-Wusong branch line of the Beijing-Shanghai Railway starts from Shanghai and ends at Fort Taiwan in Wusong Town, only four li away from the county seat of Baoshan. Moreover, the route is flat, making it easy to pave the roadbed and lay the tracks. It is estimated that ten mu of land will be needed. At a price of 200 yuan per mu, it will only cost 2,000 yuan. Adding the road construction costs, station building costs, etc., the total will be no more than about 50,000 yuan. If the route is completed, transportation in Shanghai will be closer, and land prices in Baoshan will be low, which will surely attract investment in the gold industry or the construction of residences. Therefore, a special request was submitted to the Ministry of Railways for approval. After reporting to the Ministry of Railways, it was considered that the statements were not without merit. Therefore, a special instruction was issued to the directors of the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Bureaus, Mr. Huang Bo, to be responsible for surveying the situation and submitting it to the Ministry for approval. After receiving the order, Director Huang sent two officers from the Revenue Department to survey the area near Baoshan on the previous day and consulted with the county government on everything. After the county government secretary, Bai Mingdao, described the situation in detail, they immediately returned to Shanghai to report. It is also learned that the association, in order to urge the authorities to commence construction as soon as possible, specially dispatched director Zhao Zhengping to meet with Director Huang to present everything in person. It is now awaiting approval from the Ministry of Railways, and construction will begin soon.

Japanese Ban Fujianese from Going to Japan: No Ticket Purchases Allowed 101

In recent years, Japan has been expelling Chinese sojourners from the East in numbers exceeding thousands. Scarcely a ship arrives in Shanghai without one or two expelled overseas Chinese. At the same time, restrictions on Chinese going to Japan have also been tightened. For instance, overseas compatriots doing business in Japan who wish to go to that country must first produce a certificate issued by the Japanese water police when departing Japan and returning home.

Permission to Land

Only with this certificate are they allowed to buy a ticket to board a ship. Otherwise, they are not allowed to board. Furthermore, small Chinese merchants and shop assistants (such as barbers and cooks) going to Japan must also prepay a deposit of one hundred yuan to the Japanese shipping company. If, upon arrival in Japan, the Japanese authorities do not allow the passenger to disembark and instead order them to return to China, the ship fare and other expenses will be deducted from this prepaid deposit. Such cases have been seen frequently. Recently, Japanese shipping companies in Shanghai received a telegram from Japan ordering them to

Ban Fujianese

from traveling to Japan by ship. The reason given is that Fujianese, regardless of their occupation in industry or commerce, have no fixed occupation upon arriving in Japan. Moreover, eight or nine out of ten Fujianese boarding ships in Shanghai land at Moji. This time, the ban on Fujianese going to Japan applies to all, regardless of their industry or commerce, and ship tickets are not to be sold to them. That is, they are completely prohibited from going to Moji. Fearing that some Fujianese might falsely claim to be from other provinces in order to land at other ports and enter Japanese territory, the Japanese shipping companies have added

Passenger Inspection

It is said that each Japanese ship has three inspectors who interrogate Chinese passengers traveling in third class three times during the voyage. The questions and answers are recorded in a logbook. If the answers from the three interrogations are slightly inconsistent, the passenger will not be allowed to enter the country and must be sent back to China. The strictness and precision are said to be meticulous. Local Japanese shipping companies have already complied with the telegram from Japan and are refusing to carry Fujianese passengers bound for Moji. From now on, it will be extremely difficult for Fujianese industrialists and merchants to go to the East.

The Local Weather is Cool; Yesterday Afternoon Saw Thunderstorms and Heavy Rain; Fewer Cases of Heatstroke and Heat Exhaustion; Gastroenteritis and Diarrhea Cases on the Rise 104

Since the thunderstorms and heavy rain on the 14th, the local weather has been cloudy and cool. Yesterday morning brought another heavy rain. The streets were flooded. Here is a summary of the situation:

Heavy Rain Yesterday

Since the heavy thunderstorms of the afternoon of the 14th, the local weather has remained cloudy. The weather has been cool. From 8:00 AM yesterday, there was a light drizzle. At 11:00 AM, there were several claps of thunder, and the rain suddenly turned torrential for over an hour before gradually easing. As the drainage was insufficient, the streets were flooded. The weather remained unsettled in the evening.

Disease Situation

In the past three days, there have been fewer cases of heatstroke and heat exhaustion. However, there has been a sharp increase in cases of gastroenteritis and diarrhea. This is likely due to the fluctuating weather and careless eating and drinking habits, especially eating cold foods and oversleeping, which are major causes of illness.

Zhabei Flooding

In Zhabei, low-lying areas such as Liuying Road, Baziqiao, Tanziwan, Tianbao Road, and Shunjin Lane were flooded with four to five inches of water. The houses were submerged as if in a swamp. Due to the lack of tile drainage, the water could not recede, and pedestrians had to wade through the water late into the night, much to their discomfort.

The Baishoutang Traditional Chinese Medicine Shop Bombing: What Was the Customer's Intention in Leaving the Basket? Han Abing Seriously Injured, Others Unharmed 105

Shi Deli, a native of Shaoxing, together with friends, pooled capital to open the Baishoutang Traditional Chinese Medicine Shop on Bansongyuan Road in the South City last year. The business has been operating for over a year. At around 4:00 PM the day before yesterday, a customer in his fifties, dressed in a white silk long gown and resembling a merchant, approached the counter with a prescription in hand. When Han Abing, a shop assistant, saw the customer, he immediately prepared the medicine according to the prescription, packaged it, and exchanged the medicine for money. Unexpectedly, after receiving the medicine, the customer asked Han to temporarily keep a round bamboo basket he was carrying, which contained a square tin of biscuits, saying he would return shortly to pick it up. Han, seeing that he was a customer, found it difficult to refuse and readily agreed, placing the basket in a corner of the shop. The customer left and never returned. By yesterday, he had still not come to pick it up. At around 4:00 PM yesterday afternoon, Han accidentally kicked the basket while picking up coins on the shop floor. As soon as his foot made contact, the tin of biscuits inside the basket exploded suddenly with a loud bang, shaking the roof tiles. Han's head and body were injured severely. Nearby police officers rushed to the scene upon hearing the explosion and immediately reported it to the West Gate Branch of the Municipal Public Security Bureau. They also rushed the injured Han Abing to Shanghai Hospital. His injuries are said to be severe and life-threatening. According to people in the shop, luckily, only Han was inside at the time of the explosion; otherwise, more people would have been injured. The Public Security Bureau is currently conducting a thorough investigation into the details of the case.

Execution of Opium Smoking Case: Gu Zhuxuan Imprisoned; Court Summoned Gu Yesterday for Investigation in Dai Dongpo Case; Gu Arrived in Court in Prisoner's Short Shirt to Testify 106

Gu Zhuxuan, former head of the Chan Theater and president of the Jianghuai Association of fellow townsmen from Yancheng, and Wang Xinggao, formerly serving in the military and police, both natives of Ningbo, were arrested for allegedly inciting the assassination of Tang Jiapeng. The Special Court sentenced them to fifteen years and life imprisonment, respectively. Upon appeal to the Third Branch of the High Court, the results of the trial showed a lack of sufficient evidence of the crime, and both were acquitted. Wang Xinggao was released on bail with a written guarantee of 10,000 yuan during the appeal period. The Police Affairs Department, dissatisfied with the appeal verdict, has filed an appeal to the Supreme Court. Gu Zhuxuan was sentenced to eight months in prison for bribing guards outside the Guangci Hospital prison to smoke opium. The Third Branch of the High Court upheld the original sentence and deprived him of his civil rights for one year. Now that the sentence in the smoking case has been finalized, the Criminal Execution Court of the Third Branch of the High Court ordered that Gu Zhuxuan be sent to the Second Special District Prison to serve his sentence the day before yesterday. Separately, Dai Dongpo, a Jiangbei bandit, was in the process of appealing his crime in the Jiangsu High Court in Suzhou. Coincidentally, during the January 28th Incident, he was in a refugee shelter established by Gu Zhuxuan's Jianghuai Association. Therefore, the Suzhou High Court entrusted the Third Branch of the High Court to inquire with Gu Zhuxuan about whether there was such a person as Dai Dongpo after hearing Gu Zhuxuan's appeal case on the 20th of last month, The magistrate Wang Yue asked Gu to find out if such a person existed and Gu confessed that he needed to investigate the Jianghuai Association. Gu, on instruction from the court, entrusted his brother Songmao to investigate the matter at the association and report back. Now, the Suzhou High Court has again entrusted the Third Branch of the High Court to inquire. Yesterday morning at 10:00 AM, Magistrate Wang Yue of the Third Criminal Court came to the Third Criminal Court and ordered Gu Zhuxuan to be brought to court. Gu, wearing a gray cloth prisoner's short shirt numbered 43 on his upper body and white silk trousers on his lower body, stood before the case. The official stated that he was questioning him about Dai Dongpo. Gu stated that at that time, the shelter took in many refugees, and he could not remember the names of the refugees at that time. He suggested that a letter could be sent to the office staff of the Jianghuai Association to investigate the roster, which would clarify the matter. The address of the association is now at the end of Zhongshan Road and Gonghe Xin Road in Zhabei. After verifying the confession, the court ordered the bailiff to escort Gu back to prison to serve his sentence and learned that the Third Branch of the High Court was scheduled to summon Wang Xinggao to court this morning to question him about a certain matter.

Throwing Away Elderly Mother, Wife, and Children: Tragedy in the Huangpu River 107

At 4:00 PM yesterday, a middle-aged male passenger suddenly jumped into the Huangpu River from the stern of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Shanghai-Ningbo route Xin Jiangtian steamship. His body struggled two or three times, but it was too late to save him, and he sank without a trace. The passenger was traveling with his elderly mother, wife, and one son and one daughter back home. Upon seeing this, his mother and wife were inconsolable. The French Concession Xiaodongmen Police Station took the four family members, young and old, back to the police station and notified the Customs Water Police, who sent Detective Zhou Zenghua to retrieve them. According to the deceased's wife, her husband's name was Chen Chenglong, 32 years old, from Yuyao. He had been working as a bookkeeper at the Zu'an Sock Factory on Dongyouheng Road in Hongkou. He suddenly developed a mental illness two months ago, and his speech and behavior were erratic, and he would cry uncontrollably. The illness would come and go. Today, the whole family, old and young, was traveling to Ningbo to seek medical treatment at home when he unexpectedly had an attack and committed suicide. The police chief, noting that the wife had nearly jumped into the river to seek death when she was brought back and was only stopped by the arresting officer, feared that she might repeat the attempt. Therefore, he waited for instructions to summon someone from the Zu'an Sock Factory to comfort her.

Puji Sanatorium Water Tower to Supply Drinking Water to the County 108

Since taking office, Ye Zhendong, the magistrate of Shanghai County, has been aware that the county relies on natural water for drinking water, which is unhygienic. Therefore, he recently contacted Lu Bohong, the director of the Puji Sanatorium, to connect the sanatorium's water tower to the county government. The water tower can supply drinking water to 8,000 people, while the sanatorium currently only supplies 1,000 people. Mr. Lu agreed, and the application to the provincial government has been approved. Preparations have begun to purchase two kilometers of water pipes, costing 8,000 yuan, with the sanatorium and county government each bearing half the cost. The county government will use 7,500 gallons per month, paying a water fee of 60 yuan per month. The sanatorium will handle sales to the public. The water supply project is expected to be completed within this month.

New Invention: Double-Use Security Door Lock; The Engineering Research Institute of the Academia Sinica Certifies Its Excellent Construction 109

The inclined column gate-type double-use security door lock, patented by the Ministry of Industry for five years, has been adopted by the Jiangwan Applied Science Society, which has produced six types of Arrow brand and unnamed brand door locks based on this principle, priced from 1.95 yuan to 10 yuan. The effectiveness and advantages of each lock vary. In particular, the bathroom lock, where the door handle automatically changes color depending on whether the door is open or closed, and the 1.95 yuan unnamed brand tumbler double-use door lock are the most ingenious and unique. These door locks have also been tested by the Academia Sinica, which has certified that the lock doors are within the NX range and that the tooth shapes of the keys are different for each lock, with the same effectiveness as the popular foreign "Yale" and "Corbin" locks on the market. Furthermore, it has been proven that the entire structure has three major advantages: A. The simple construction reduces costs, resulting in a low selling price; B. All parts are uniformly strong, ensuring durability and preventing sudden damage; C. Prevention of water ingress and rust, taking considerable care in this regard. The locks are currently sold by Fengyuan Trading Company at 356 Beijing Road, as well as by Yong'an Company, Sincere Company, and major hardware stores.

The Telephone Company Will Issue Another Notice to Subscribers Regarding the Reporting of Bills and Documents; This Concerns Your Vital Interests, Please Do Not Abandon Them 110

The Telephone Problem Committee of the Shanghai Special District, in preparation for negotiations with the Municipal Council to request that the council, based on the terms of the franchise agreement, convene a board meeting to re-discuss reducing telephone rates if the income of the Shanghai Telephone Company exceeds 10%, has issued a notice to all telephone subscribers in the city to promptly report their recent new fee bills to the committee. It has been more than three months since the committee requested subscribers to report their bills, and the number of bills reported by subscribers has been small, making it difficult to conduct a comprehensive audit. Yesterday, another notice was issued, urging them to promptly report the bills for verification. The notice is recorded as follows: Regarding the issue of negotiating the increase in telephone rates in the Special District, the Chinese Ratepayers' Meeting of the Public Concession resolved (1) to collect all relevant evidence, (2) to ensure that the profit does not exceed 10%, and (3) to calculate profits based on actual equipment. A letter was sent to the committee to collect new bills from subscribers and forward them for auditing so that a proposal could be submitted to the Municipal Council for rediscussing and lowering telephone rates. The committee issued a notice and sent a letter to the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce to instruct all businesses to comply. However, since more than three months have passed, the number of reports received by the committee has been small, making it difficult to conduct a comprehensive audit and proceed with negotiations. Therefore, another notice is hereby issued, urging all telephone subscribers in the city to promptly submit all new bills and evidence of floating calculation figures to the committee (Shanghai Special District Telephone Problem Committee, located within the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce at Tianhougong Bridge) within the latest time limit so that they can be forwarded to the Chinese Ratepayers' Meeting for protest. This matter concerns the interests of all Chinese and is a struggle to control the benefits of public utilities. Please comply with the reporting requirements and do not delay.

North District National Products Promotion Week Begins Today 112

The North District National Products Promotion Week of the National Products Year National Products Movement will begin at 2:00 PM today in the lecture hall of the Shanghai North District National Products Exhibition Hall on North Sichuan Road. The ceremony will be grand, with the Liang sisters unveiling the curtain. There will also be entertainment. The order of events is as follows: 1. Ringing the bell to start the meeting; 2. Reports by staff on the situation of the Shanghai North District National Products Exhibition; 9. Entertainment.

Conference Staff

The staff of the Promotion Week conference has been determined as follows: presidium members Yuan Ludeng, Wang Xiaolai, Yu Zuoting, Zhu Gengtao, Xu Xiaochu, Chen Jicheng, Zai Manyun, Zhou Bangjun, Wang Hanqiang, Cao Zhigong, and Zhang Yi; master of ceremonies Ge Futian; secretaries Tao Leqin, Zhu Yutao, and Zhu Yangwu; general manager Liu Zhongying; reception Zhu Yunqing, Chen Jiufeng, Sun Yinfeng, Chai Guojun, Wu Hezhang, and Dai Qian. The venue is the responsibility of Liu Mengfei and Wu Gechang, who are in charge of the decoration.

Venue Decoration

The Promotion Week is attached to the Shanghai North District National Products Exhibition Hall, located on North Sichuan Road, in a newly built two-story, bright, and sunny building. At the entrance, there are three tall arches decorated with national flags and painted in bright colors. Inside, there are five pavilions decorated with pine and cypress trees, with two entrances and four exits. The horizontal banner of the Shanghai North District National Products Exhibition Hall hangs above. The venue is luxuriously decorated, clean, and beautiful, with ample light and fresh air. The pedestrian path is ten feet wide, so there is no fear of crowding. Emergency fire extinguishers are hung everywhere, and the Three-Section Fire Brigade has sent a fire truck to the venue to maintain safety. The North Station Branch has dispatched police officers to be stationed at the venue. The sales area is in a long snake shape, leading to the lecture hall at the end. The lecture hall is full of alarming slogans and is very grandly decorated.

Robbery of a Large Quantity of Cigarettes: A Night of Searching Leads to False Alarms; Bandit Den Uncovered in Nanhui County; Stolen Cigarettes Hidden in the Home of Pan Xukui, Head of Xiukang Township; Head of Township Flees with Entire Family, Several Tables of Food and Drink Still Set Indoors; Stolen Cigarettes, Totaling Twenty-Seven Boxes, Discovered Buried in a Graveyard; Idea for Cigarette Robbery Came from Crew Members of Yizhong Tobacco Company's Cigarette Transport Ship 113

The Yongtaihe Tobacco Company of this port, on the evening of the 27th of last month at 7:00 PM, hired barge number 20702 belonging to a Ningbo man named Wang Ahu, to unload various brands of cigarettes produced by the Yizhong Tobacco Company, including Little Fairy, Red Seal, Golden, Pinhai, Old Knife, Red Tin Package, and the Huacheng Tobacco Company's Golden Rat and Maoling brands, totaling thirty-nine boxes, from the company's warehouse on the south bank of the Zhabei Road Bridge in Suzhou Creek. These were to be transported to various sales locations of Wusong Zhang Yuanmao, Xiang Dalong, Lao Tongsheng, Tonghexing, and Yongtaihe distribution points. The barge arrived at

Qiujiang Wharf near the river surface, close to midnight. Suddenly, a wharf boat loaded with bandits approached and docked alongside Wang's boat. Ten bandits jumped out, brandishing handguns, and threatened and bound the master and crew members with ropes, locking them inside the cabin. They then proceeded to move the cigarette boxes onto the bandit boat, stealing a total of thirty-seven boxes, worth 6,060 yuan. Remaining were one box each of Little Fairy and Old Knife brands. The bandit boat then sailed away. Yongtaihe Company immediately reported the incident and dispatched personnel to request the assistance of the Customs Water Police in pursuit, and also

placed a notice in the newspaper offering a reward of 500 yuan, hoping for public cooperation in apprehending the criminals. On the 7th of this month, the Water Police learned that the cigarette robbers were crew members from several of Yizhong Tobacco Company's cigarette transport ships, all of whom had fled and disappeared. On the evening of the 12th, they received a tip-off about the bandits' whereabouts and, on the morning of the 13th, dispatched detectives, together with officers from the Pudong Branch Bureau, to apprehend three cigarette robbers from Chongming, Sheng Dalang, Shi Yinlang, and Gu Erlang, in a shed behind the Labor Village near the Branch Bureau. There was also a fugitive from Zhenjiang next door, Wang Jinsheng,

who had fled upon hearing the news, with only his wife, Wang Zhangshi from Yangzhou, being captured. The four suspects, both men and women, were taken to the Branch Bureau for interrogation and detention. On the morning of the 14th, they were transferred to the Water Police, where they confessed that the stolen goods had been transported to Zhou Pei and Zhang Cailin, because Zhang's family ran a general association, making it easier to sell the goods. Upon hearing this confession, the detective head immediately dispatched five experienced detectives, Cheng Yongnian, Shen Changshan, Hu Changqing, Qu HeKui, Gu Wenkui, etc., at 1:00 PM, along with one of the Sheng suspects, to

Zhoupu Town in Pudong, to cooperate with the police from the First Resident Police Station of the County Public Security Bureau in arresting Zhang. According to Zhang's confession, after the stolen goods arrived in Pudong, they were transported by Shen Jialu, Wu Jiasheng, and Wang Baoming, all from Beicai. The detectives then escorted Zhang to number 62, section seven of Beicai Town, and apprehended Shen Jialu and Wu Jiasheng. They were taken back to the police station, where Wu Jiasheng confessed that he was the Deputy Commander of the Xiukang Township Defense Corps in Nanhui County. According to both suspects, the stolen goods were initially transported to the NanChang Paper Shop near the Huanlong Bridge in Datuan Town,

but after failing to sell them, they were returned and transported by Wu to the home of Pan Xukui, the Township Head of the Sixth Bao of Xiukang Township. As a result, the case became increasingly complicated. The original detectives then cooperated with the Head of the Zhoupu Defense Corps, accompanied by four members of the corps and two officers from the First Resident Police Station, to escort Wu overnight to Pan Yongzhai's house in Qiujiage, Xiukang Township, the home of Township Head Pan Xukui, for a search. As they approached Pan's residence, it was already midnight.

They heard the sound of gongs being beaten loudly, followed by a dense barrage of gunshots. The detectives, unaware of the true situation, huddled in the fields to observe the situation. After a while, when the gunshots subsided, they learned that a Cai family residence in the area had been robbed. The villagers had sounded the gongs to gather a crowd to pursue the robbers, who resisted by firing guns as they fled. Once the detectives' panic subsided, they continued forward and arrived at Pan Xukui's residence, which turned out to be a huge complex of more than twenty interconnected rooms. The doors and windows of each room were open, and there were

several tables of food and drink still warm in the reception hall, but there was no one to be found. The detectives then entered the house with their guns and searched the premises. They soon discovered an empty room in the rear, with numerous box marks on the floor and a piece of crate recovered, bearing the name of the Yizhong Tobacco Company. The detectives tracked the trail to the rear bank and observed that the duckweed in the bank was disturbed, as if a large object had been thrown into it. At this point, it was clear that the Pan family had fled with the stolen goods upon hearing the news. They then discovered a sack of cigarettes hidden in a

field near the house, containing eight boxes of Pinhai brand cigarettes in packs of fifty, four boxes of Red Seal brand, one box of Old Knife brand, eighteen pieces of crate wood, and the words "Pan Xukui" painted on the outside of the bag. In addition, there were five carrying poles, indicating that the stolen goods had been transported away. On the 15th (the day before yesterday), after dawn, the Water Police received a report and dispatched additional detectives, Zhou Zenghua and Xu Lenian,

to assist. At around 8:00 AM, a villager reported to the Zhoupu First Resident Police Station that a large quantity of cigarettes was hidden in a graveyard about 150 yards east of Township Head Pan Xukui's residence. Because the surrounding area was surrounded by dense trees, it was difficult for outsiders to notice. The detectives rushed to the location and uncovered one box of 36 packs of Maoling brand, one box of 185 boxes of Golden Rat brand, one box of

76 boxes of Old Knife brand, one box of 28 boxes of Pinhai brand, one box of 53 boxes of Golden brand with 300 packs, nine boxes of 176 boxes of Red Seal brand with 73 packs, and six boxes of 96 boxes of Little Fairy brand with 470 packs, totaling 27 boxes. All of the boxes were extremely damp. It appeared that the remaining ten boxes had already been sold. The stolen goods were transported back to the police station for temporary storage. The detectives then searched again all night the night before last, until yesterday morning,

when the entire team of detectives brought the Sheng Dalang suspect back to Shanghai. Zhang Cailin, Shen Jialu, and Wu Jiasheng, the three suspects apprehended in Nanhui County, were escorted by the police station to the County Public Security Bureau for disposition yesterday. The Water Police then notified Yongtaihe Company to join them in Nanyi today to transfer the three suspects and the stolen goods for investigation and prosecution. The police also learned from the confessions of Sheng Dalang and other suspects that

the idea of the cigarette robbery had been in the works for a long time. The first attempt was about three weeks ago, when they secretly used boat owner Yang Maotou's wharf boat number 5728 to intercept the original cigarette transport ship, but they were unsuccessful. The second time, they used Yang Maotou's wharf boat number 5272 to wait at Qiujiang Wharf and successfully rob the cigarettes. They sailed the boat to Qichang Warehouse in Pudong and hired a new Fei tugboat to tow it to the Bailianjing port, where they sailed into Zhoupu, etc. Yesterday, the police also impounded the two boats mentioned and are awaiting instructions.

Private Opening of Letters Results in Fine 114

Lu Zhongwen, Ye Liang, and Chen Zhengzhou from Guangdong, the inventors of the three-purpose light bulb, entered into a contract to establish the Central Three-Purpose Light Bulb Factory at 221 Sapo Sai Road in the French Concession, with Ye as the factory manager, Chen as the general manager, and Lu as the deputy. Last month, Lu, Ye, and others discovered that Chen had falsified the accounting books, leading to a dispute. Accountant Wang Zikang was appointed as a mediator. On the 4th of this month, during negotiations at Wang Zikang's home, Chen discovered that Lu had secretly opened and read letters sent to him from Hong Kong, leading to an argument. Chen reported this to the Public Concession Police, who detained Lu and notified the French Police. Detective Jin Bingwen brought Lu back and sent him to the Special Second Court. The French Police Department filed a public prosecution against him for both obstructing privacy and theft. The defendant, Lu Zhongwen, argued that the plaintiff, Chen Weizhou, had established the Central Three-Purpose Light Bulb Factory in Hong Kong without his consent, infringing upon the inventor's interests and constituting a breach of trust, so he took the letters as evidence. After investigation and trial by Judge Qiu Huan of the Special Second Court, a date was set for sentencing. Lu was ordered to provide bail and be available for summons. Yesterday was the date of sentencing. At 8:00 AM, Judge Qiu delivered a judgment in the Eighth Criminal Chamber, finding Lu Zhongwen guilty of opening and concealing another person's sealed letter without reason, and sentenced him to a fine of twenty yuan. If he failed to pay, he would be required to perform labor service, with one yuan equivalent to one day. He was found not guilty on the other charges. Upon hearing the verdict, Lu expressed his dissatisfaction in court. The court ruled that the defendant must remain on bail pending the appeal period. It was also heard that Lu Zhongwen had filed a complaint with the Criminal Division of the Special Second Court accusing Chen of forging documents and breach of trust, and a hearing would be held soon.

Foreign Automobiles Coming to Shanghai Can Obtain Temporary Concession Permits - Must Be Applied for Through the China Automobile Association - 116

The China Automobile Association, after lengthy negotiations, has obtained permission from the Shanghai Public Concession and French Concession authorities to issue temporary permits to foreign automobiles for short stays in Shanghai. The fees for these permits have been set at two yuan in national currency for the first three days, with an additional one yuan for each subsequent three days (or less). The total stay in Shanghai cannot exceed thirty days. In addition, there is a one-yuan fee for a driver's license. Since the implementation of this new temporary permit system, it has been well-received by various sectors. Foreign automobiles can now easily come to Shanghai and drive around for a short stay without having to obtain a six-month automobile permit. However, these temporary permits must be applied for through the China Automobile Association. If they can be obtained, they are the right of the members, because all foreign automobiles staying in Shanghai are guaranteed by the association with cash deposits that they will return to their original place of registration on time and that all automobiles will pay the fees as required. This method was originally initiated by the association, which aims to develop the Chinese automobile industry and makes every effort to contribute to society in any way that benefits the public. It is believed that the two concession authorities welcome and support Chinese and foreign automobiles coming to Shanghai for sightseeing, as China has now opened its doors wide to automobile travel. The association hopes that the Chinese government authorities will recognize the permits issued by the governments of various friendly nations for automobiles, so that automobiles from all countries can freely come to China for travel and sightseeing, just as the concession authorities allow Chinese mainland automobiles to travel in the Shanghai concessions, providing convenience in order to promote China's tourism industry. The association has recently submitted a request to the Chinese government authorities to achieve this goal.

Western Body Found on Avenue Dubail: Murder or Suicide Yet to Be Determined 117

The Shanghai Evening Post & Mercury reports that this morning (the 16th), a young man's body was found on Avenue Dubail, not far west of Avenue Haig. The man had been shot in the head. It was later learned that the deceased was an American, Mr. Covert. There was no weapon found near his body, so investigators today believe the man was murdered, not that he committed suicide. However, it is also possible that it was suicide. Around 3:00 AM this morning, a sentry at the Lancashire Barracks on Thibet Road heard a gunshot nearby, but could not see anything in the dark. Then, around 4:15 AM, a rickshaw traveling along Avenue Dubail found a man lying on the sidewalk north of the road, about 960 yards west of Avenue Haig. The rickshaw driver reported the incident to the Chinese police at number 276 nearby, who then notified the Avenue Haig police station by telephone. An ambulance arrived and took the man to a nearby rural hospital. Mr. Covert was not yet dead at that time. Doctors confirmed that he had been shot in the head and provided treatment, but he died of his injuries at 9:26 AM. At the same time, the Avenue Haig police station began a thorough investigation. Based on the condition of the injuries prior to death, the deceased had been lying on the ground for at least an hour before being discovered, so he had been shot at least an hour earlier. Police searched the dead man's pockets and found his passport, which revealed his name and that he was 36 years old. There were seven copper coins in his pocket. At 6:30 AM, they reported the incident to the American authorities, who ordered the body to be transferred to the International Funeral Parlor on Kiaochow Road for a preliminary examination. It was found that the bullet had entered near the right temple and exited the back of the head. The deceased was from the state of Utah in the United States. It is heard that he came from a famous family and married in Honolulu. The couple arrived in Shanghai about a year ago, but have not found employment. Not long ago, he went to Yantai once. When they first arrived in China, they had a large sum of money, but it has now been mostly spent. The couple has been living at 150 Thibet Road. This morning, his wife said that her husband returned home around 2:00 AM last night, and she and him went to visit a friend at 52 Avenue Dubail, but did not enter the house. Her husband gave her about 100 yuan and left, and that was the last time she saw him. She also said that her husband had a handgun that he had been trying to sell recently, but he had not found a buyer. She does not know the caliber of the gun, and the gun is now missing.

Qingliang Temple Eviction Case: Qinghai Sues Sheng Yuyou, Alleging Perjury Before the Judicial Authorities; Defendant Has Gone to Study in England and Cannot Respond to the Lawsuit 119

The abbot of Qingliang Chan Temple at 15 Xinchang Road, Qinghai, is seventy-three years old. Last year, he was sued by the British merchant Tonghe Yangxing, represented by a lawyer, in the Civil Division of the First Special Court, requesting eviction. The reason given was that the original site of Qingliang Temple at 15 Xinchang Road was the property of the late Qing Gongbao Sheng Xuanhuai's wife, Zhuang Laotaitai, and was leased by Qinghai for a term of five years. If Qingliang Temple added buildings or other structures on the vacant land, they should be

completely demolished after the expiration of the term. Later, in 1928, the Sheng family borrowed 150,000 taels of silver from Tonghe Yangxing and mortgaged the houses and vacant land at that location, transferring the property deed and all property rights. Later, Tonghe Yangxing, considering that the houses were old and in need of repair, planned to rebuild them, and therefore notified the Qinghai monk in writing in September 1934, giving him a deadline to move out. Because they could not get what they wanted, they filed a lawsuit. As a result, the first instance judgment ordered Qinghai to move out of the houses located at 15 and 16 Xinchang Road and

return them to the plaintiff. This case was not allowed to be provisionally enforced. Later, the defendant appealed the judgment, and the third and final instance has concluded, with Qinghai losing the case and now in the process of enforcement. Now, Qinghai alleges that Sheng Yuyou, the descendant of Sheng Zhuang, committed perjury before the judicial authorities, so he has hired two lawyers, Lu Qi and Yuan Xilian, to file a complaint with the Criminal Division of the First Special Court, stating that when Tonghe Yangxing sued Qinghai for eviction, the defendant in this case, Sheng Yuyou, was clearly the landlord and one of the parties who signed

the lease in question, yet he did not file a lawsuit himself in accordance with the law, but colluded with Tonghe Yangxing, the manager, to file a lawsuit with the court and gave false testimony twice in court. For example, on the afternoon of January 29, 1935, in the Thirteenth Court, he testified that the land in question was initially mortgaged to Tonghe Yangxing for 150,000 taels of silver in 1928 and later increased to 350,000 yuan, and that the land in question was about twenty mu, including the house, and that the property title was also handed over to

Tonghe Yangxing. However, according to Tonghe Yangxing's complaint, the initial mortgage was 200,000 taels and now it has been increased to 350,000 yuan, and the land in question is twenty mu, three fen, four li, and five hao, and Tonghe Yangxing only has the mortgage right, not the ownership right. Because of Sheng Yuyou's false statements, the plaintiff in the original case lost the lawsuit, which constitutes the crime of perjury under Article 168 of the Criminal Law, etc. This case was heard by Judge Tan Xinzhen in the Eighth Criminal Chamber at 11:30 yesterday morning. The defendant, Sheng Yuyou, hired Xu Shihao and Zuo Detao as lawyers, who stated in court that Sheng Yuyou had gone to

England to study last August, and all the documents from the previous case have been forwarded by the Chinese Ambassador to England, so it is impossible for him to appear in court. Moreover, this case has already concluded in the third instance and is now in the stage of enforcement, and the plaintiff is aware that the defendant is far away overseas, but intentionally filed a lawsuit to confuse the court and presented the judgment. The plaintiff's lawyer, Lu Qi, said that although this case has already concluded in the third instance, Qinghai is still filing a lawsuit for execution objection and confirmation that the contract is invalid, etc. Judge Tan said that he needed to review the files from the previous case to investigate whether the defendant had gone abroad, and then ordered a change of date for further verification.

Expansion of the Gongxin Accounting Firm 120

The Gongxin Accounting Firm was founded in February 1934 by Accountant Xi Yushu, assisted by Accountants Chen Chaolun and Cao Yu. The firm's name, Gongxin (public trust), was chosen because the accounting business places the utmost importance on creditworthiness and should be trusted by the public. However, in the initial stage of its establishment, all external matters were still conducted under the name of Accountant Xi personally. Now, Shen Weijing, Chen Zongshun, Zhu Xinmin, Zhang Genglin, Li Haopei, Yao Fuyuan, and other accountants and lawyers have joined the firm successively. It was originally planned to move into the Zhongshi Building on July 1, but for the convenience of registering creditors, the firm has expanded at its original address in the Jinxing Building at 509 Nanhe Road. In terms of internal organization, Accountant Xi will serve as the chief accountant, with Cao Yu as the director of general affairs, Gong Maode as the deputy director, Shen Weijing as the director of audit, Chen Chaolun as the deputy director, Chen Zongshun as the director of schools and editing, Zhu Xinmin as the deputy director, Li Haopei as the director of the legal department, and Yao Fuyuan and Zhang Genglin as lawyers and accountants. In the future, all external matters will be conducted under the name of the Gongxin Accounting Firm. Accountant Xi has been practicing in Shanghai for ten years, and he has always been serious and highly reputable in handling cases. Now, with the assistance of many scholars, its business prospects will definitely be even more promising.

The Truth About the Prohibition of Yellow River Flood Relief Lottery Tickets 121

The Shen Times News Agency reports from this port that recently, newspapers reported that the Executive Yuan had issued an order to stop the issuance of Yellow River flood relief charity lottery tickets. At the same time, the Yellow River Flood Relief Lottery Office published a notice stating that they would continue to issue the tickets, which had been filed with the Executive Yuan by the Hebei-Chahar Political Council. A reporter from the Shen Times News Agency interviewed the Ministry of Finance and other related parties to clarify the truth and learned that the Executive Yuan had previously approved the issuance of the tickets up to the twelfth issue. When the thirteenth issue was continued, the Hebei-Chahar Political Council did submit a request to the Executive Yuan for filing. The Executive Yuan forwarded it to the Ministry of Finance for review. The Ministry of Finance replied that the issuance of the lottery tickets had been approved previously as a temporary measure and should not be continued. The Executive Yuan then issued an order to the Hebei-Chahar Political Council to stop the continued issuance of the tickets as discussed. The Yellow River Flood Relief Lottery Office said that it had filed with the Executive Yuan, but in fact, although it had submitted a request, it had not been approved. Currently, the tickets are still being sold in Hunan, Hubei, Shanghai, and other places. The governments of various provinces and cities have successively sent telegrams to the Ministry of Finance asking whether to ban them and requesting a reply. The Ministry of Finance replied that the tickets had not been approved for continued issuance by the Executive Yuan and issued separate telegrams to ban them in accordance with the law. This is the origin of the statement that the issuance has been stopped.

Gaoqiao Rural Association Establishes Daycare Centers 122

Since last year, the Gaoqiao Rural Improvement Association has successively established agricultural busy season daycare centers in Xiling, Xingang, and other places, assigning female teachers to be in charge of all matters, including training, education, and care. This has reduced the mental burden on farming families and provided educational convenience for children. With the help and assistance of the Gaoqiao Health Office and local people, the project has made further progress. Therefore, public opinion is in favor and the results are remarkable. This summer, in addition to the two existing centers, two more centers have been established in Gaoxing and Gaoqiao. Mr. Wang KuiSheng, the director of the association, also consulted with the China Children's Welfare Association, which agreed to provide a subsidy of 600 yuan for start-up costs for the establishment of the Gaoqiao daycare center and to supplement other centers. Children aged two to six can register to join. Admission and departure from the center are based on certificates with photos attached to ensure formality. The Gaoqiao Town Daycare Center is located in the park, which has a beautiful environment. Shuttle buses are used every day to pick up and drop off children in the morning and evening, and the facilities for naps, showers, games, etc. are also very complete. At present, the number of people in each center is quite developed. This project is still new in the Gaoqiao area, and future progress depends on the continued efforts of local organizations and enthusiastic people.

A New Scam in Shanghai Involving the Sale of Shotguns and Radios: Forged Seals Used to Collect Letters, Claiming Letters Not Received; When Police Investigated and Went to Make Arrests, the Company Had Moved Away; Zhang Wenwei, Who Was Visiting to Investigate Ways to Make Money, Detained by Detectives 123

Zhang Wenwei, Wang Xu, Wang Xihua, etc., from Danyang, opened a Central Company inside Dahua Bookstore and Haoyundao Bookstore at 40 Jiaotong Road, specializing in the sale of shotguns, radios, etc., at particularly low prices. Those from other places who needed to purchase the above items only had to mail the money to the company, and the goods would be delivered immediately. Because of the low prices, the business was quite developed, and many people from other places sent money to purchase the items. Recently, it was discovered that the seals on many registered letters sent to the company were forged. The Central Company also contacted the post office to ask why so many letters had not been received. The post office investigated Huang Guozhen, the postman who delivered the letters to the company, number 450. According to Huang, all the letters were indeed delivered to the company, and the company personnel signed for them and provided the seals. He did not know whether the seals were genuine or not. The post office then sent an employee, Zhang Guangshu, and others to investigate, but no evidence was found. The case was reported to the Hongkou Police, and Chief Detective Xi dispatched Chinese detectives Huang Fusen and Lie Zhaonian to investigate. For several days in a row, there was no news. The day before yesterday morning, Detective Huang, disguised as a student, went to 40 Jiaotong Road. When pretending to buy books, he happened to hear two apprentices from the Central Company talking. They instructed each other that if postal or police personnel came to investigate, they must firmly claim that the letters had not been received and that no other information could be revealed. Detective Huang thought that the words of the apprentices were very suspicious, and that it was obviously a scam. He reported this to Chief Detective Xi and obtained a search warrant from the Special Court. In the afternoon, he went to the Central Company to search, but the company had moved away, and none of the responsible personnel could be found. The case was finally revealed, indicating that the company had forged its own seals to collect the mail. When customers questioned, they would answer that they had not received the money, in order to achieve their fraudulent financial goals. After strict investigation, it was learned that Zhang Wenwei lived at 2 Fangxie Road. An arrest was made, but he was not found. It was also found that all of the company's assets had been moved to the Renxing Postal Transport Company at 32 Chungen Lane, Edo Road, and were impounded. Unexpectedly, Zhang Wenwei went to Jiaotong Road in the afternoon to investigate the situation. He was spotted by the detectives on guard and arrested. Zhang denied the incident, saying that he needed to find Wang Xu (also known as Tongsheng) and Wang Xihua before he could know the truth. The detectives then went to 96 Anlan Road with the police detectives from the Public Security Bureau to arrest Wang and Wang, but they were not found. Yesterday morning, Zhang was sent to the Fifth Division of the First Special Court. The police lawyer Qian Xunjiu stated the previous situation. Because the police still needed to investigate and arrest the remaining suspects, he requested permission for detention. Judge Fu Lin questioned Zhang Wenwei and ordered that he be detained and interrogated again in a week.

Arrest of a Chinese School Tea Boy on Suspicion of Robbery: Water Police Detectives Allege His Involvement in the Robbery, But Whether He Was at School at the Time Requires Further Investigation 124

On the 6th of last month, Shanlian Town, Wuxing County, was raided by a large gang of Anhui-籍 pirates, with losses amounting to over 40,000 yuan. At the same time, dozens of rifles were stolen from the security team. Subsequently, the Water Police Corps seized two ships in Jiaxing and other locations, apprehending several bandits and confiscating more than ten firearms. The fifth squad of the first brigade of the Water Police Corps also cooperated with Chinese Detective Feng Zhiming of the Shanghai Public Concession Police to capture three bandits in Shanghai, who have already been taken back. Now, Wang Qirong, a detective from the fourth team of the Water Police, also an Anhui native, happened to be in Shanlian Town when the bandits raided it, and many of the bandits were known to him. Among them, there was a bandit from Anhui named Wu Changhou (also known as Changnian), who he knew was working as a tea boy at the Shanghai Chinese Public School. He then accompanied a Zhu-姓 police officer to Shanghai. Because they did not know the location of the Chinese Public School or Wu's whereabouts, they took a trolley bus at 1 PM the day before yesterday, intending to visit Xiaoshadu Road to inquire. Unexpectedly, when the bus passed Avenue Road, they saw Wu walking on the road. They immediately got off the bus and, with the assistance of Chinese Constable No. 2942, arrested Wu and took him to the Chengdu Road Police Station. Yesterday morning, he was escorted to the eighth criminal court of the First Special District Court. Zhang Tianyin, a lawyer from the police station, requested permission to detain Wu temporarily, stating that the defendant had been working as a tea boy at the Shanghai Chinese Public School of the Public Works Department on Jingzhou Road for many years. According to Wu, he did indeed take a month's leave between April 27th or 28th and May 29th, but he returned to school on May 29th, meaning he was at school on June 6th. The period of leave is the key to this case, and the police station still needs to investigate, and so on. When questioned, Wu Changhou denied the allegations. Judge Tan Xinzhen reviewed the confession and ordered him to be detained for further questioning at a later date.

Suspicious Death of Liu Dianlong's Wife and His Unwillingness to Allow an Autopsy: The Court Orders an Examination Before Releasing the Body for Burial 125

Liu Miao-氏, a 33-year-old woman from Yangzhou residing at No. 6, Xinglongfang, Lane 101, Chongqing Road, was found the day before yesterday with her hands and feet discolored and her condition critical. Her husband, Liu Dianlong, was informed, and he accompanied her to Renji Hospital. After examination by the hospital's doctor, it was determined that she had ingested opium, and an enema was administered, but to no avail. She soon died. The hospital reported the matter to the Chengdu Road Police Station, which dispatched detectives to investigate. The body was then taken to the Philander Road Morgue for examination. Yesterday morning, Zhang Zongru, a prosecutor from the First Special District Court, along with forensic doctor Zhang Yan and clerk Wang Zuyi, etc., arrived at the morgue to examine the body. Head Constable Jiang Linxiang reported the previous circumstances, and Liu Dianlong, the deceased's husband, stated that he was 33 years old, from Yangzhou, and had been a detective in the French Concession Police for two months, but now worked at a dance hall in the Albert Garden. At 5 AM yesterday morning, I finished work and returned home, where I saw my wife lying on the floor smoking opium. At 1 PM, the maid told me that my wife had suddenly fallen ill. When I went to see her, I noticed stains on her trousers. I then called Dr. Chen Jiuzhou of Chinese Medicine for treatment. He prescribed medicine. Later in the evening after I arrived to the dance hall, my family rushed to me, reporting that my wife's fever had worsened. I rushed back and saw that her hands, feet, and other parts of her body were purple. I then sent her to Renji Hospital. That hospital immediately recognized it as a drug overdose. Without even taking her pulse, they performed an enema. As a result, she died within fifteen minutes of arriving at the hospital. I know that those who treated her were not doctors, and my wife and I were very fond of each other. There was no reason for her to take her life through suicide. Therefore, I suspect if she indeed died from a drug overdose or she died from illness, I have doubts, so I ask for a detailed examination to determine the cause of death. After hearing the statement, Zhang-君 said, "If you have any doubts, then the body must be dissected for examination before a determination can be made." But Liu refused. Zhang-君 then ordered that the deceased, Liu Miao-氏, female, was indeed poisoned to death before death. The body was handed over to her husband, Liu Dianlong, who signed a statement to claim it for burial.

Smuggling Ring Case Involving Two Section Chiefs of the Police: Defendants Charged Under the Statute for the Punishment of Smuggling and Tax Evasion Claimed They Refused at the Time; Trial Concluded Yesterday 126

Liu Shu'en, Chen Yousan, Zhang Baoren, Chen Shaoqing, Wang Daosan, etc., chiefs of the fourth section of the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway police on the Shanghai-Xihu line, allegedly opened a room at the Quancheng Hotel near the Shanghai North Station in April of this year and invited Ma Rongqi and Yao Changtai, former policemen, to discuss the formation of a smuggling ring for copper coins and rayon. This was discovered by Chen Tiemeng, chief of the section, who reported it to Zhong Jianhun, the head of the section. The police were ordered to arrest Liu Shu'en, Chen Yousan, Zhang Baoren, Chen Shaoqing, etc., and detain them at the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway Police Department. Yao Changtai, Ma Rongqi, Wang Daosan, etc., fled. They were immediately transferred to the District Court, where Prosecutor Lei Binzhang completed the investigation and prosecuted them under Articles 1, Section 4 and Section 5 of the Statute for the Punishment of Smuggling and Tax Evasion (both of which carry the death penalty). As public officials, they should also be punished more severely in accordance with Article 134 of the Criminal Law. Yesterday, Judge Zhao Yongzhou opened the trial. Liu Shu'en, Chen Yousan, Zhang Baoren, Chen Shaoqing, etc., stated that they had served in the railway bureau for periods ranging from two to three decades. Although former policeman Yao Changtai had solicited them, they refused. Chen Tiemeng had made a false report to curry favor, and they requested a clear judgment. Thereupon, Prosecutor Lei issued his opinion, believing that the facts of the crime were proven. Finally, lawyer Zhang Yongqing defended them at length. The presiding judge announced the end of the debate and scheduled a date for sentencing.

"No More Prickly Heat," A Good Medicine for Summer 127

Prickly heat is prevalent in summer, causing unbearable itching. If the skin is scratched and broken, bacteria can enter easily, causing sores and boils. Because sufferers are numerous and treatment is lacking, the healer is responding to the needs of patients. Based on his experience, Dr. Fu Zhuangmin of this city has created "No More Prickly Heat," a special product for treating prickly heat. Since its release, all who have used it have found it effective and without side effects. It is cooling and delicate, and after application, it feels like a gentle breeze, gradually relieving the prickly heat. "No More Prickly Heat" is not for profit, so there is no separate distribution point. It is prepared and sold by Dr. Fu's clinic at Lianzhuli, Avenue Road. The price is only 20 cents per large package.

Ms. Zheng Wenmei Returns to China: China's First Female Railway Expert 129

Ms. Zheng Wenmei, from Yuyao, Zhejiang, has a Bachelor of Education degree from Shanghai University. She served in the Shanghai-Nanjing-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administration for three years. She was highly regarded by the authorities for her capable work. In the autumn of the 24th year of the Republic, the Ministry of Railways gave her the preferential treatment of retaining her position and salary, and entered the University of Pennsylvania in the United States to study railway transportation. She also interned in personnel management and railway accounting at the Pennsylvania Railway and the New York Central Railway. She graduated this summer with a master's degree. Ms. Zheng is indeed the first person in China to study railway transportation as a woman. It is reported that she has returned to China on the 15th of this month.

Painter Chen Nanhe Passes Away 132

The famous painter Chen Shanyu, pen name Nanhe Shanren, from Wuxing, was a distinguished student of Zheng Wenliao of Beihai. He was intelligent, skilled in calligraphy and painting, and had a reputation in the art world for many years. Recently, due to the increasing number of people seeking his work, he overexerted himself and fell ill. Despite treatment by famous Chinese and Western doctors, medicine was ineffective, and he passed away at his Shanghai residence on the day before yesterday (the 14th). Chen's family is in dire straits. He left behind a son and a daughter, both underage. However, he had a rich collection of calligraphy and paintings during his lifetime, including works by contemporary celebrities Yu Youren, Tan Zekai, and the late Tan Yankai and Hu Hanmin. Chen's relatives and friends plan to display these treasures and other valuable paintings in Dr. Cheng Jinghan's medical office at No. 25, Le Lane, Tangyou Road, for public viewing, hoping to sell them to raise funds for the living and education expenses of the orphans.

Weather Report 134

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday stated: Shandong is cloudy to sunny, with southeast to northeast winds. The upper and middle reaches of the Yellow River have light winds with indefinite directions. The upper and middle reaches of the Yangtze River are cloudy to overcast, with thunderstorms and unstable winds. The lower reaches of the Yangtze River have fog and northeast to southeast winds. The hurricane north of Paro Island is still moving northwest-west. Its center at 2 PM was within about 120 miles of 10 degrees north latitude and 135 degrees east longitude. Wind force is unknown. Also, the highest temperature in Shanghai in the 24 hours before 3 PM yesterday was 81.3 degrees, and the lowest was 75.9 degrees. On the same day last year, the highest was 98.1 degrees, and the lowest was 76.5 degrees.

Letter to the Editor 135

To the esteemed Editor,

I am writing to you because I recently read in your newspaper, on the third page, twelfth edition, an article titled "Overseas Chinese Merchant Chen Bingding Discusses Improving Agricultural Food, Planting Cassava and Mountain Millet." I was delighted to read it. (Omission) In addition to being happy, I am planning to try planting a small amount first. However, it's hard to get seedlings and seeds in abundance. Mr. Chen is warm-hearted and benefits the people, and it might be helpful if you could first go collect them so that small numbers of people who have ambitions may have the convenience to buy seeds. I don't know Mr. Chen's address. Please lend me a corner of your newspaper to publish this, and I hope Mr. Chen can reply.

Sincerely,

Lu Meichu

(Address: No. 32 Xingsheng Street, French Concession, Shanghai)

Education News

Ministry of Education Actively Plans to Establish National Model Secondary Vocational School: Entire Plan Drafted; Basic Vocational Subjects to Be Offered First 137

In the national budget for the 25th year of the Republic, 850,000 yuan was allocated for productive education expenses. 300,000 yuan of this amount was designated for subsidizing well-run secondary vocational schools. The subsidy standard is being comprehensively planned by the Ministry of Education. The remaining 550,000 yuan is designated for the establishment of a national model secondary vocational school. It has been reported that the entire plan for the establishment of this model vocational school has been drafted. The Ministry of Education, the Sino-British Boxer Indemnity Fund Board of Trustees, and the Beijing Municipal Government will discuss and finalize the arrangements, and then actively proceed. The school will be located in Nanjing, and basic vocational subjects will be offered first, such as civil engineering, mechanical engineering, applied chemistry, and electrical engineering. This year, land acquisition, construction, and other matters will take time. It is expected that basic practical subjects will be offered first to the greatest extent possible, and a full range of subjects will be offered after the summer vacation next year.

Education Director Wang Discusses Employment of University Graduates: Government Has Decided on Various Measures 138

Ping Zongquan, Quan Nai'sen, and others from various universities went to the Ministry of Education on the morning of the 15th to present their views on the employment of university graduates. Minister Wang received them and spoke for over an hour. It is said that the response was very satisfactory. The main points of Wang's speech were as follows: Regarding the employment of graduates from specialized schools and above, the government has been thinking about solutions for years. As for what the government has decided, (1) the Executive Yuan has consulted with the Examination Yuan and decided to hold an examination in mid-September. The number of admissions will be greater than in previous years, and the Executive Yuan will guarantee distribution of appointments. (2) Regarding performance evaluation of civil servants, the government has now decided to eliminate 2% of civil servants with poor performance each year and recruit university graduates through examinations to achieve renewal. (3) Regarding employment training classes, the classes are scheduled to begin on October 1st, with a temporary enrollment of 1,000 students. Graduates who pass the examination and are in good health can be recommended by their respective schools. The government has plans for their future career paths. Finally, there is one more thing that is very important to report to everyone, that is, the highest authorities of the government are fully determined to solve the service problems of graduates from specialized schools and above. In the future, all those who pass the examination or receive training and have excellent performance will be absolutely and forcibly employed by the various agencies under the highest government authority.

Examination Results for This Year's Graduates: The Bureau of Education Directly Distributes to Each School; Each School Will Carefully Calculate Graduation Scores and Report to the Bureau of Education Together with Graduation Certificates 139

The Shanghai Bureau of Education announced yesterday about public and private secondary schools and normal schools in the city: The graduation examination for students in secondary schools and normal schools in the city for the second semester of the 24th year of the Republic was held on June 22nd and 23rd respectively. The exam papers for each subject have been graded. All examination results are now being distributed to each school by the Bureau. Then the schools will calculate the grades based on the new regulations published by the Bureau for this year's graduation examination for students in (senior high school), (junior high school), and (normal school), articles (18, 19), (17, 18), and (18, 19), and will fill out and report to the Bureau of Education with the graduation certificates before the end of this month, to make it verified. Do not delay, and urgently notify. This notice,

The contents of articles 18, 19 and 17, 18 of the newly promulgated senior high, junior high and normal graduation examination regulations are as follows:

(1) The method for calculating the grades of each subject in the graduation examination shall be based on 40% of the school's graduation grades in each subject and 60% of the examination grades in each subject. The aforementioned grades are all calculated as percentages. Decimals below the integer shall be rounded off. 80 to 100 points is grade A, 70 to 79 points is grade B, 60 to 69 points is grade C, and less than 60 points is grade D. Grades A, B, and C are passing, and grade D is failing. (2) Each school shall fill out the graduation grade summary table issued by the Ministry of Education separately. As for the graduation examination grades for each subject, after the examination is completed, the results of the examination will be notified to each school by the Bureau, and the schools will fill them out and calculate them in detail, and submit them to the Bureau with the graduation certificates for verification and printing.
