The School of Business of Shanghai University's downtown campus recently launched a discussion conference on commercial education. School News 147

Liangcai Vocational Supplementary School: The Liangcai Vocational Supplementary School, affiliated with the Minhang Songhu Memorial Guangci Hospital, specializes in accepting elementary school graduates for one year of rigorous vocational training. The courses offered are all tailored to practical writing applications in preparation for employment. This summer, the first graduating class of the school had more than 20 students, and various factories and businesses competed to select suitable trainees. Except for a few students with poor grades, most were introduced to jobs by the hospital. It is recently heard that the school will not openly recruit students from the next academic year. Those who wish to understand the nature of the school and are willing to enroll must have elementary school grades of average or above, be physically strong, have good character, and be able to endure hardship. After passing the examination, they can be recommended by the original school and admitted without examination. The tuition fee is 50 yuan per semester, and all required books and materials are provided by the hospital.

Guohua Middle School: The private Guohua Middle School, located at the intersection of Robert Road and Gordon Road in this city, will establish 50 scholarship positions from the next academic year to cultivate outstanding and impoverished students. Regarding facilities, efforts are being made to achieve perfection. Recently, a large-scale construction project has been undertaken to add three large classrooms. Regarding academic subjects, knowledgeable scholars have been hired as full-time teachers. The school has scheduled July 20 as the date for the new student entrance examination, and many people have been enthusiastically registering in recent days.

Mrs. Huffman Teaches English: Mrs. Huffman, an Englishwoman, graduated from a famous British university and has been a teacher for many years. She now teaches conversation, grammar, composition, translation, etc., at home, and also provides translation and writing services for various documents. She is also willing to guide those who aspire to enter various levels of schools at home and abroad. The tuition fee is very low, and both group and individual instruction are available. Mrs. Huffman currently resides at 455 Lafayette Road, Apartment 207, near the French Garden.

Nanjing National Academy of Drama: The National Academy of Drama is the first art specialty school in China to be established with state funds to study dramatic arts and cultivate theatrical talents. The principal, Yu Shangyuan, is a theatrical expert who has studied in Europe and America for many years. The school will begin its second enrollment in the fall of this year, with 30 places available. Both male and female students are accepted. Those with junior high school qualifications and dramatic talent are eligible to apply. Tuition and lecture fees are waived. For a brochure, please write to the school at No. 8 Xuejia Lane, Nanjing. The registration deadline is from July 15 to August 10.

The International Leisure and Entertainment Conference will be held in Hamburg from July 23 to 30. The conference is international in nature, and its value and importance are worth introducing. Now, in order to entertain thoughtfully, we have prepared 40,000 single and double rooms - the facilities are very perfect - so Germans and people from all countries can come to Hamburg to participate in this unprecedented event, and there are trained guides there, who are under the management of the general affairs department of the conference, to do their best to serve, and there will be no any difficulties."

Yesterday, the US cotton market opened, and the news from Liverpool and Mumbai was not good. Liverpool, the Far East, the Mainland, and Wall Street sold off. The weather report was favorable, and each month fell by 12 to 16 points. Then, local merchants and fellow merchants bought in, and the market situation rebounded strongly. Before the close, long positions settled and cotton farmers hedged, and then it softened again. It is estimated that spot fell by 13 points, and futures fell by 10 to 13 points. Spot goods are scarce and strong, and the textile market is lively. English cotton spot fell by 14 points, and futures fell by 9 to 10 points. Indian cotton long positions settled and operators dumped, which was absorbed by large short positions. European exporters bought in on dips. It is estimated that Pingguoer rose or fell by 0.25 to 2.25 Robbie, Aomla fell by 3.75 to 4.75 Robbie, and Bailuo Creek fell by 3.5 Robbie. The original telegram is recorded on the left (telegram dated the 15th).

According to a Mumbai telegram, the opening forecast for the Bai Luo Creek cotton for the April-May period on the 16th was 225.5 Robbie, up 0.75 Robbie from the previous day.

According to an Osaka telegram on the 16th, the price of Sanpin futures yarn fell by 4 corners to 1.3 yuan, with the near-term month at 212.9 yuan and the forward month at 206.8 yuan. The price of cotton futures rose by 25 cents to fall by 45 cents, with the near-term month at 72.4 yuan and the forward month at 65.45 yuan.

Silk and Tea: The Silk Yarn Market Still Shows No Improvement 165

Yesterday, the overseas silk market mostly retreated slightly. The New York Japanese Hua silk price fell by 2 cents per pound. The spot price of White Factory B character 78 degree fell by 1 cent yesterday, and the futures price fell by 1.5 cents. Yokohama spot price rose by 1 yuan, and the futures price rose by a small 4 yuan. Lyon Japanese silk rose by 1.5 francs, and the rest showed no ups and downs. In the domestic silk market, the meal sales have not yet turned around. Hangzhou sources have a strong sense of confidence and are actively purchasing. It is said that in addition to some loads sold to Shanghai, there are also many people from various villages who have heard the news and directly transport them for sale.

Piece Goods: Cotton Cloth's Trend Suddenly Weakens; Local Merchants' Purchases Decrease and Shrink; Fine Cloth and Fine Twill Both Decline 168

Yesterday, the cotton cloth market situation was because spot yarn and cotton and foreign cotton continued to fall, and although various merchants and the local street had greatly absorbed them during the previous frenzy, actual transactions did not improve. Therefore, store owners' hand goods and some of the surplus blank cloth quotas from dyeing factories are quite willing to sell. Because the situation in Guangdong is unstable, the large amount of this factory's fine twill absorbed before still has a profit of 3 to 4 corners per piece in the current market, and they are now being transferred out in Shanghai. Because of these several layers of pressure on the market, although the factory plate is still solid, the trend has suddenly weakened. The prices of local fine cloth and fine twill fell, but only 5 cents to 1 corner per piece, the price of city cloth 84 fell 1 corner per piece, the price of this factory's fine twill fell 1 to 2 corners, and the price of bleached cloth fell 1 corner. Because the previous increase in prices for local fine cloth, coarse cloth, and coarse twill was moderate and there is a lack of spot fine cloth, the selling plates have not been changed. The purchases of various merchants and local streets have been greatly reduced.

Metals, White Lead Sheets Drop Both Domestically and Internationally 176

Yesterday, due to the rain, the metal market was slow. The offerings included only 300 loads of English steel plates, 20 barrels of white lead sheets, and over 200 bundles each of corrugated iron and galvanized iron wire. Other items with limited trading included new iron wire, tinplate, company iron, small-sized nails, and nails from local factories. The price of galvanized iron sheets dropped because of the overseas telegraphic reports of falling prices. In the Shanghai market, No. 2 sheets were sold at $140 per barrel, No. 3 at $134, No. 4 at $132, No. 5 at $128, Nos. 6 and 7 at $127, and No. 8 and thicker patterned sheets were offered at $123-124. The increase was about $0.50 to $1.50 less than before. Overseas prices were quoted at £17 10s per ton, a decrease of 10s from before. It is heard that fellow traders have booked orders for 300-400 barrels, anticipating a further drop in market prices in the coming days. In addition, the prices of old iron and other items remained stable due to limited trading.

Shen Bao Literary Supplement

Red Nose 177

— Shen Shengshi

It was a bit of a surprise to see that burly old man with the red nose again in a small, half-open shop on the ancient Hulong Street, sitting foolishly at the doorway, smoking a water pipe, and watching over a small candy stall.

I was somewhat astonished that the red nose had changed so much.

Seven or eight years ago, when I was in middle school, there was a time when a few companions and I were very interested in learning to carve seals. Every Saturday and Sunday, we would go to the shops on Hulong Street that bought and sold old cultural relics to buy some cheap seal stones. At that time, the red-nosed old man had a very respectable antique shop in another area of Huyou Street. There were glass cabinets lined up at the door, and he had many antique collectibles. We often went to his shop to buy seal stones. He had more seal stones than other shops, but the red nose was very temperamental. When you went to buy things from him, you often had to put up with his arrogant manner of speaking.

We only bought inferior stones that cost a dozen or so copper coins each, but the red nose often thought that such small business was a nuisance to him. Sometimes he would deliberately take out stone seals that cost two or three yuan each and tell us that he also had ones that cost dozens of yuan each. His face turned as red as a tomato, and he would sniff his red nose, pinching the fleshy lump on the left side of his cheek repeatedly. His eyes, filled with red veins, would widen, and his purplish-red lips would tremble. He would always impatiently say to us:

—Trouble, trouble, you only buy such cheap things. If you want good ones, buy the ones that cost two yuan and five jiao each. They are really good seal stones.

We often went to his shop to bother him and always did small business of about one mao (tenth of a yuan). His way of speaking always looked down on us. A few times when we went there, he would just smoke his water pipe and ignore us. After we greeted him, he would impatiently sniff his red nose and take out some of the worst hard stones.

Later, we didn't want to bother him with his bad temper anymore. One reason was that we were busy with schoolwork and didn't have time to be distracted by those small hobbies. Another reason was that we had spent a lot of money, but our carving skills hadn't improved. Moreover, the graduation exam was approaching, and the problem of finding a job after graduation was still unresolved. So, we no longer had the leisure to put our hearts into the small hobby of carving stones.

From then on, we no longer went to the red nose's antique shop. Occasionally, when we passed by his shop, we would see him leisurely smoking in the glass cabinet.

After leaving middle school, we groped aimlessly in society for a living. For many years, sorrow and indignation filled our hearts, and the mood for learning to carve seals that we had in those years was long gone.

Carrying the sorrow of unemployment, I returned to the ancient city. Unexpectedly, I saw that red nose again. I never thought that the big-shot antique shop owner would be so down on his luck now. His once-respectable antique shop had closed down, and he had moved to such a small, half-open shop. The red nose had been defeated by life and had even started a small candy stall business.

I stopped blankly for a while by that candy stall. The red nose probably didn't recognize me. How could he know that I had also returned to the ancient city carrying the sorrow of being defeated by life!

Hope 178

— Tang Tao

It was only the beginning of spring.

After several days of rain, a northwest wind blew, and it cleared up. The threshing ground, which had been trampled by chickens and ducks, was full of footprints. The low-lying areas were still flooded with water, and the river was also full.

Near the pier, a boat was tied with a cable. Old Jinshui stood on the pier, sending off his two sons, who were taking shovels, earth baskets, rakes, brooms, and other soil-moving tools onto the boat. They planned to go to town to collect garbage today.

Every year, the farming families in the village have to put a little fertilizer in the fields. They can't afford fertilizer powder, and even human manure is considered too expensive. The fertilizer they usually use is garbage ash, which is made by piling up garbage into a small mountain and setting it on fire. It smolders for six or seven days until it is all burned into ash, which is used to fertilize the fields. This is the cheapest fertilizer. However, most of the people in the village are farmers, and poor families usually can't bear to throw things away, so there isn't much garbage. They have no choice but to go to town to collect it.

After the tools were secured, the boat pushed off from the shore.

Near the surface of the pond, a thin layer of ice had formed. Sanbao held the scull, and Sixi and Old Jinshui sat at the bow of the boat. The boat was light, and the river water was high. It rocked from side to side very badly. Sometimes the boat got close to the pond, and the ice scraped against the edge of the boat, making a rustling sound.

It takes a long time to go from the village to town by water. Old Jinshui smoked his pipe and chatted idly. The lines etched on his dry face explained his hard experiences, a great resume.

The boat was like a drunkard, staggering forward. Old Jinshui talked with great enthusiasm.

"Hey! You were just children then! Abao was only four years old, and you were still nursing. It was the first year of Xuantong. The sun was really poisonous that year. The cracks in the fields were a foot wide. The disaster was as bad as last year."

Old Jinshui paused here, took a few puffs of his pipe, and continued:

"But the second year was a good year. The early rice grew to half our height, and we harvested more than four bags. The two seasons made up for the losses of the first year. I turned things around that time."

Erbao stopped sculling, letting the boat drift on the water. He listened almost entranced, not even noticing the oncoming boat. By the time he heard the shout "Boat coming, keep to the side!", it was too late to turn, and the two boats bumped heavily into each other. After hearing the ferryman on the other side grumble, the boats went their separate ways.

"Does that mean this year will be a good year?" Sixi asked.

"Yes, the old saying goes, 'The first eight days are sunny, a good year!' The first eight days of this year were good weather. And it snowed all winter last year."

The flame of hope burned in Old Jinshui's heart, burning in Sanbao's heart, and in Sixi's heart. Happiness, like spring grass, sprouted in this dead, gray wilderness.

"If that's the case, we have to buy our own cow, so we don't have to borrow from this family and that family and still have to watch their faces," Sanbao suggested.

"And I have to make a set of white cotton short shirt and trousers like my brother," Sixi also said his long-awaited wish.

Old Jinshui smiled. Ha! Ha! Ha! He tapped the ashes out of his pipe on the edge of the boat, refilled it, and smoked it. His eyes contained the glow of warm hope, like that of a young man waiting for his lover. He was so urgent and so full of happy premonition that he completely forgot last year's disaster, forgot the days of hunger and cold.

Sanbao took off his short cotton jacket and shook it vigorously. The sun slowly rose, and the boat sculled closer and closer to its destination.

By the time they arrived in town, it was already noon. The vendors selling fresh goods had already left the market, and the streets were damp. The father and sons ate some dry rations they had brought with them in the boat. They picked up their collection tools and jumped ashore.

Several of the shops in town were closed, some with large red papers pasted on them, and some with white-bottomed black-character strips. But most of them were still open. The shop assistants leaned against the counters, idly watching the pedestrians on the street. There were two streets in the whole town, with about a hundred shops in front and back. On odd-numbered days, farmers from the surrounding villages would come here to the market, and fishermen from the coast would also bring some fresh goods to exchange for money, so some business would still come to these shopkeepers. But in recent years, the shops in the eyes of the farmers have gradually become showrooms. They strictly adhered to the motto "Only allowed to visit, not allowed to touch." They didn't buy anything because they couldn't afford it.

The more sluggish the business in the shops, the more they wanted to attract buyers. They hung up big "discount" flags in front of their doors and beat gongs and drums. The sound of the gongs and drums conveyed a desolate and empty tune, but it still sounded lively at first.

This excitement made Sanbao and Sixi feel interested. They collected garbage while watching the scenery, like watching the City God's Fair in the second month. The windows of the foreign goods store displayed exquisite household items; the snack shop constantly emitted the aroma of travelers' saliva; the foreign cloth store hung various kinds of clothing. When Sixi thought that as soon as the beginning of autumn came, he could pick out a fine piece of clothing here, the garbage he was carrying on his shoulders suddenly felt lighter.

Old Jinshui urged them on, but he was also very happy. The reason for his happiness was that after a few days of rain, there were not many people coming to town to collect garbage, so the garbage had accumulated very high. In previous years, they had to go door-to-door to ask, but this time, it came right to them, which was very convenient. This convenience seemed to foretell a good harvest this year. Plenty, abundance, Old Jinshui had already foreseen the days when he would turn things around again.

Because they loaded a little more, it was evening before they had a full boat. Tired bodies wrapped in excited hearts, they washed their hands, feet, and the scull stirred the river water, and that's how they started their return journey.

The garbage was full, containing coal ash, rags, animal bones, and fish scales. These things, burned into ash and used to fertilize the fields, were very nourishing for the rice. They can make the rice grow quickly and form heavy ears of grain, which can be exchanged for money, bought cows, made white cotton shirts and trousers, and built up a golden harvest from these.

This boat full of garbage is a boat full of hope.

The one sculling was still Sanbao. Old Jinshui held his pipe and sat at the bow of the boat, his eyes looking at Sixi's back as he pulled the rope on the shore. The setting sun on the west mountain, with a touch of red light, slowly faded away. Everyone only ate a little dry rations at noon, and after a day of labor, their stomachs were rumbling, so they were especially eager to get home. However, the garbage had been rained on, and the weight was quite considerable. The heavier the boat's draft, the slower it rocked, and the louder their stomachs rumbled.

"I'm starving!" Erbao said.

"For the sake of future fullness. You must be patient," Old Jinshui put down his pipe. "This year's garbage is plentiful and good. Buried in the fields, it's sure to be a good harvest!"

"We should have brought more snacks and a lantern. Look, it's already getting dark!"

As Sanbao said this, he perked up and started to scull harder. The boat began to move from side to side. This force was transmitted from the tow rope to Sixi on the shore, and he also pulled harder. The boat did indeed move a little faster. The waves at the bow of the boat splashed high, like tens of thousands of bright pearls jumping.

Old Jinshui was so tired that he closed his eyes, wanting to doze off.

Although more than half of the journey had already passed, the sky became even darker. A few sparse stars were nailed to the grayish-blue sky. The distant villages were submerged in the misty night. The air in early spring was quiet. Sanbao tried his best to scull. The side of the boat closest to the water was originally only two or three inches away, but at this time, with the boat tilting, water poured in mouthful by mouthful. Hunger made people impatient, fatigue made people careless, and the dark night obscured people's eyes and people's conscience.

Sixi on the shore felt that the tow rope was getting heavier with each step, but he thought it was because he was too tired from working so hard during the day. So he put all his strength into pulling desperately. After a few steps, with a "snap," the tow rope broke, and Sixi rushed forward.

"Ah!" Sanbao cried out.

Old Jinshui was startled and opened his eyes, only to see a vast expanse of white. The bow and stern of the boat were still exposed on the surface of the water, but the garbage in the middle cabin had already drunk its fill of water. It took the grain, the cow, the white cotton short shirt and trousers, the abundance, the fullness, the hopes of these three father and sons, and sank slowly along with the boat.

Petrel 179

— Xijin

——Rereading Gorky's poem on January 20

The petrel is flying in the sky again,

Flapping its wings and suddenly soaring;

A long and loud cry,

A bright figure, crossing the sky,

Reflected in the dark and gloomy sea...

The gale roars on the water,

Churning up towering waves:

Heavy rain strikes down the weak white seagulls,

The dark clouds in the sky turn and crush out

Thousands of lightning bolts and deafening thunderclaps;

The petrel loves to fly in its storm,

The more it flies in the turbulent waves, the more courageous it appears,

Flying over the waves, flying over the foot of the clouds,

In the struggle, it shows off its invincible joy!

The shrinking clear water crow is swallowed by the white waves,

The shores where the penguins hide are also washed away;

The triumphant petrel shouts out a prophecy of victory:

"After the storm, there will be clear weather ahead!"

Finished Fishing 180

— TK

Gambling 181

— Zigang

Whenever there was a yellow wind blowing for a day or deep snow, Old Zhong didn't want to force himself to the street to do business. His stall was moved from the street corner to the front of his own courtyard, and the small screen wall became a natural windbreak. Under the blue cloth top, Old Zhong's black cloth vest shone. His hands were red and swollen as he pulled the dough, like arranging an array. He segmented it on the pressing board. The little moustache was covered with condensed breath, flashing in the dim sky light. He shivered again, and his heart cried out for cold.

"More sesame seeds!"

"Be careful, don't bake it too burnt or too tender. If it's not crispy, it's not formal!"

"Put more sesame seeds, it's fragrant!"

Even though it was a business of two copper coins each, the customers were still troublesome and picky with him.

Old Zhong didn't even raise his eyes to talk back. He blew up the sparks that were about to go out from the wind, rolled the sesame seed in the sesame seed, looked up at the top of the canopy, and then lowered his head again. People also temporarily closed their mouths.

"Old Zhong, why were you so unlucky last night, ha ha ha!"

"Yesterday, that hand of cards wouldn't fight with me. Nian Chang San, leave Yao Er... that's enough!"

The "Black Zhang Fei" from the coal shop across the street or the partners who pulled the monthly (carriage) came to find the old man, yawning.

The hunched black vest straightened up suddenly, shaking off two drops of water stuck on the top of his moustache. Old Zhong wiped his nose with the oil-stained sleeves. "Damn, I don't know what's plaguing my heart. I'm just having bad luck. Don't even think about getting a good hand. Alas, I'm old and worthless! I, with my bad eyesight, picked the wrong card on the ground. It's my fault for playing it wrong..."

Old Zhong burst out laughing from the bottom of his heart, wanting to wipe his hands with his apron and straighten his back to have a "chat", but couldn't resist the urging of the people beside him. His loud voice shook like a clumsy camel bell in the wind and snow:

"Okay, can't you wait a while? Isn't our old story good? The bad one last night will definitely be 'better' tonight. I, Old Zhong, will win at least once in ten hands. I dare not boast about anything else! Old Zhang Fei, you wait, tonight, Brother Xiang and the others will peel your skin..."

Old Zhong's "ha ha ha" was drowned out by the reprimands of the customers.

The widowed woman Wang from the west entrance liked to recite a passage:

"Old Zhong is really a fool. He's been a bachelor his whole life, sending all his money to paper cards and pai gow. Doesn't he have an acre of sorghum land at home that he doesn't plant? Old Zhong, isn't that right? No brothers, no nephews, I'm saying, isn't he a fool, giving away the ten or so strings of money he earns with his ten fingers to the black charcoal guys every day!" She twisted her head, examining the "qian'er" (a kind of hair accessory), and went west, very happy to express her opinions. This stirred up a burst of laughter:

"Why don't you talk, Brother Zhong! Are you afraid of talking and playing?"

"Old Zhong is shy," said someone, probably the pockmarked sister-in-law, lightly adding, "Brother Zhong has never been near a woman in his fifty years!"

"Just buy the sesame cakes, that's all. Why chat about eighteen strings of things? Chatting about 'gambling' is not far off, but it's always about women, no children..." He turned red with anger, and his big hands, stained with sesame paste, waved back and forth: "I, Old Zhong, had no life to marry when I was young. Who's to blame? When I was strong, I could barely fill half my stomach. Who's to blame? Now, what's enough with a few strings left? My head is bald too - who's to blame?" He took advantage of a moment of free time to dry his hands and light a dry cigarette:

"Why don't you let me rest and look at the cards? I say - why? I've suffered all my life, I've worked hard all my life, and I should take a breather! I suffer and get angry in other things, only on a few cards, I call the shots; I pick whoever I pick; I discard whoever I discard, just like I've been pulled and pushed by people for decades," he chewed and savored it repeatedly like betel nut: "Pulled, pushed, beaten, scolded... Oh, more than fifty years..."

Everyone knew that Old Zhong had carried a gun, worked as an apprentice, and performed tricks, until a month before selling sesame cakes, Old Zhong was still sweating profusely on the street, begging for money from the spectators. But when he was unexpectedly disappointed, he angrily cursed and didn't show his face for a few days.

Under everyone's serious silence, Old Zhong suddenly laughed wildly, and some of the shadows in his heart were driven away by this tearless wail. He saw the blue sky outside his blue canopy again. The old man's felt boots moved loosely a few times.

He would subconsciously arrange the pieces of dough into dots on playing cards or dominoes, sighing to himself:

"Plum blossom pair! Heavenly bar is coming, wonderful! Oh, what a pity! Bring another one..." He went into thought.

Beside the candied haws wooden basket, he would also stop, squeezing his eyebrows and smoking. When the children played marbles on the ground, he would also listen:

"Old Zhong, are you coming, one big coin a game! Let's fight!"

This old fellow would be coy at first, and if there were not many adults around, he would clumsily squat down slowly. He would forget himself clapping his hands. He cleared his throat and shouted, as if saying: It's my turn to pick you and push you!

There were a few days when Old Zhong automatically stopped working, which was when there were weddings or funerals nearby. Among the group of drummers and coffin pullers squatting on the ground playing pai gow or dice, Old Zhong sat on the ground like a big Buddha, staring at the dice, his big hands patting on his legs.

When he had lost all his money and business was slack for a while, Old Zhong would take out a deck of cards and play against himself on the pressing board, putting down one card with his left hand and picking up one with his right hand, moving sesame seeds back and forth to determine the outcome.

He was still muttering:

"I pick you, and I can say I don't want you, you, dare to say no!"

"Like this, this will come fairly, and everyone has nothing to say, fairly! The world of the bastards is not fair!" He swallowed the last sentence.

Offering Books 182

— Cao Juren

—One of the Random Picks—

The Palace Museum is restoring the Qing Dynasty literary inquisition archives. There are many tragedies and many comedies. To say that those who broke the law, who really wanted to rebel against the Qing and restore the Ming, and become national heroes, seem to be few; most are like "Zhu Maichen" characters, who want to covet temporary wealth and offer books, but cannot get their wish. It is quite interesting that they then offered their own annotated versions of the Book of Poetry and the Book of Changes to Emperor Qianlong, hoping that the emperor would act as a matchmaker for them and grant them an "Imperial Mandate Wedding." Among them, the most pitiable and tragic ending is the case of Ding Wenbin's Great Xia Great Ming New Book.

Ding Wenbin, a native of Shangyu, Zhejiang, grew up in Hangzhou. During the Yongzheng period, he lived with his elder brother and sister-in-law in Songjiang for more than ten years. His brother and sister-in-law were very poor and made a living by selling cakes and doing odd jobs, but they did not expect this good brother to cause them big trouble. In May of the sixteenth year of Qianlong, Ding Wenbin went alone to the Duke Yansheng's mansion in Qufu, Shandong, to offer books (the Great Xia Great Ming New Book and the Zhaowu Reign Era Almanac). He said that when the old Duke Yansheng was alive, he had promised to marry his two daughters to him. Besides the marriage, he also wanted to pass on the throne. The special commissioner interrogated him severely. Let's take a look at his confession:

Question: "You are from a humble background, and now you look like a beggar. How could Duke Yansheng be willing to marry you? Moreover, there is no reason to promise two daughters to one person, and there is no matchmaker. This is obviously a false accusation!"

Answer: "My marriage is by the order of God, so why need a matchmaker? One husband and two wives are the way of Yao and Shun. Shun married Yao's two daughters, which is well-documented. The old Duke Yansheng was no different, so he passed the throne to me and married his two daughters to me. This was all inspired by God. I heard that Duke Yansheng had passed away, so I took over the throne, and it has been eight years now. Because no one helps me, I don't even have food to eat... The people in the South do not understand the great truth. They don't pay attention to me, so I had no choice but to write this book..."

Question: "How did you make him the Holy Emperor and send drafts to the women of the Kong family? Who is the daughter of that Dong family? Confess everything!"

Answer: "God's will is always that those with virtue have position. The old Duke Yansheng was able to uphold the way of Yao and Shun, so he should be in the position of Emperor. I was taught the way of Yao and Shun by the Holy Duke, as if he passed the throne to me, so I respected him as the Holy Emperor in the book and also called him the Artistic Ancestor. In the past, when Shun received the throne from Yao, he also called him the Artistic Ancestor. The book containing a mother-in-law and wife was all written by myself, and I did not send it out, and I don't remember which year it was... The book also said that Dong was to be a concubine; that Dong family is from Songjiang, her father is called Dong Hengshan, who runs a tea house. I had no food to eat, so I helped him fan the bellows for half a year. Seeing that his daughter was only fifteen years old and looked good, I thought in my heart and recorded it in the book."

Question: "In your book, you made Kong the eldest uncle the Grand Secretary, and Kong the uncle the Grand Minister of Rites, and Kong the uncle the Grand Minister of Education. What are their names? You also made your elder brother Duke Wen of Xia, and your parents King and Queen. Where were they enfeoffed? Did you have any edicts or other items for them?"

Answer: "Kong Lei is the Duke Yansheng. The officials and original investigators were all from the Kong family, so I casually recorded what I wanted to grant. My elder brother's name is Ding Wenyao, and my sister-in-law Qin sells sesame cakes in Songjiang. This year, he is helping in a noodle shop. He is a person who does not understand reason and often scolds me for being crazy, so I said in my book that my brother is stubborn and my sister-in-law is arrogant. Because I took the throne, I should treat him with courtesy, so I wrote it in the book."

Question: "You also forged six copies of the Almanac. How dare you write the words 'Imperial Decree' without authorization? You have been falsely claiming to be on the throne for eight years. Why are there two copies of each item, only six or seven...?"

Answer: "I only have one person writing and copying books. Because God ordered me to rush to revise this Great Plan of the Spring and Autumn Annals, I could not have the time to create this new book. It was not until the sixth year of my enthronement that I started to create it, and I only created it for three years. Great Xia is my country name, and Tianyuan is the reign era. Because I did nothing good, I asked God last year to change Tianyuan to Zhaowu and pass the throne to the Little Holy Duke. Since there is a reign era, I wrote Imperial Decree. As for writing 'Great Xia' and 'Great Ming' on the cover of the book, it means to cultivate virtue; 'Great Xia' means to implement the time of Xia."

This matter is very clear. The memorial of Yang Yingju, the governor of Shandong, also said: "Ding Wenbin is a person of extreme poverty and lowliness. Once he learned a little bit of old sayings, he boasted himself as a genius and exceptional talent, unmatched by anyone. Because he fantasized about wealth, noble women, and lust, his delusional mind grew stronger and could not be broken. He肆肆(transliteration error in source material)indulged in his fierce heart, howling like a wolf and barking like a dog, stopping at nothing." However, the ending of this event was not to treat Ding Wenbin as a mentally deranged person. In June of the eighteenth year of Qianlong, Ding Wenbin was executed by dismemberment by imperial decree. In September of the eighteenth year of Qianlong, his son Ding Wenyao, nephew Ding Shixian, and Ding Shilin were sentenced according to the law and should be beheaded after the autumn. Still, the son under the age of fifteen, Ding Shiliang and Ding Shiwei, were sent to the Ministry to become slaves. Wang Suxing saw the rebellious book and did not report it, so he was punished with one hundred strokes of the bamboo and exiled three thousand miles according to the law. Cai Yingda and Xu Xuchu mixed up to read the heretical book, each punished with eighty strokes of the bamboo. This meaning is very clear: the "sage and wise" Emperor Qianlong used Ding Wenbin, this madman, as an example of "killing the chicken to scare the monkey," so that everyone would not dare to hide rebellious books or shield rebellious people; that is to say: seeing a rebellious document, one must report it.

This comedy ended here, and the Great Xia Great Ming Emperor and Duke Wen of Xia and his son were sent to the execution ground together.

Page 18

Era Medicine Publication

How to Become a Healthy and Beautiful Woman A Letter from a Girl 183

Editor:

I am a girl who pays the most attention to hygiene, and I always dream of becoming a healthy woman. Unfortunately, my physique is the opposite. Not only is my development small, but I am also far from meeting the conditions for health and beauty. This is the regret I have had for several years! Banning Private Schools from Over-Enrolling Students 189

— Jianping

The number of private elementary schools in this city is alarming. Therefore, there is the vulgar name of "Lane Elementary School." These types of "Lane Elementary Schools" are nothing more than a few speculators who intend to make a profit and then open such schools. Financial difficulties and the lack of talent have led to simplicity. The school has become a business store, and even the current social education system has been completely destroyed. It is even more unnecessary to hope that it can teach ordinary children to become good and useful talents. However, simplicity is still a school. Unfortunately, the scholars who run this kind of "Lane Elementary School" often turn students into goods or private property due to business competition. They use all means to buy, deceive, and win over. Once a student steps into the school gate, it is like the target of the "school merchants." They will not let you out of the school gate, unless you pay the tuition and all kinds of exorbitant taxes and fees, you will not be allowed to pass. In terms of "doing business" skills, this type of "school merchant" can be said to be very outstanding; if you talk about education, or making students aware of the current national society in times of crisis, survival, and life and death, only God knows.

Recently, the Municipal Education Bureau has also noticed the ugly and nauseating aspects of this type of "Lane Elementary School." According to the local news on the 12th: The Municipal Education Bureau, in view of the various bad behaviors of private schools, has a great impact on the entire education of this city. Therefore, it has strictly formulated three measures to ban them — 1. Schools shall not solicit students by improper means. If there is any incident of using teachers from neighboring schools to induce students to transfer, once verified, they will be banned without leniency. 2. Teachers who are employed within the unexpired period shall not transfer to other schools without the permission of the original principal. 3. If there are bad teachers who instigate students to transfer schools arbitrarily, once there is conclusive evidence, those who have registered will have their registration revoked, and schools shall not employ those who have not registered. Schools that employ such bad teachers shall be severely punished.

It is our great good fortune that the education authorities can pay attention to the fraudulent activities of this type of educational scum and do their best to strictly ban them. Among the three banning measures currently promulgated, what we are not satisfied with is that it is limited to the phenomenon of "soliciting students" and has not found that there are still many bad phenomena in this type of private school. However, the beginning of a thing is often not perfect. Of course, we cannot be too demanding. On the contrary, we only hope that after one thing is effective, we can more thoroughly understand the destruction of education by the general "school swindlers" and "school merchants" and ban them.

These three measures do not seem to be perfect either. The reason is that the focus is entirely on "bad teachers," while neglecting the proactive actors — those who take money out to run schools, aiming to earn back a sum of money, those types of guys who are nominally school directors, principals, or something. If there were no various inducements from them, I believe that ordinary teachers may not be "bad." Therefore, we advocate strictly banning the "school merchants" and "school swindlers" who are in charge, which is a more effective method. If the main culprit is not convicted, but the accomplices are convicted, this will always be a mess.

Finally, we also advocate taking active measures to ban this type of "Lane Elementary School." The method is to improve the school education itself and not allow it to have the slightest shortcomings, so that the "school merchants" and "school swindlers" will not have a chance to "take advantage of the loopholes."

Seeking Employment 190

— Shi Jida

I've written to several places where I might find a job, but haven't received a reply in ages. In the nearby areas, I always manage to scrape together a meager amount of travel expenses, taking buses or boats, or even walking, to visit relatives and friends, begging them to get me into some organization where they could secure a job to sustain my livelihood.

"My hopes are very, very small," Liu Jin thought, "just enough meager salary to avoid starvation."

However, society is facing rural bankruptcy and cities are suffering from anemia, shattering even Liu Jin's small hope. There are so many unemployed people that the competition for jobs is becoming increasingly fierce, creating extreme difficulties for someone like Liu Jin with his social standing.

"Brother," he would say things like, "I've been unemployed for a year now. If I don't find a job soon, not only will I be in trouble, but my whole family will starve!"

Although the other party holds great sympathy, the answers are always vague and confusing.

"Brother, wait a little longer and see."

"Maybe there will be something, maybe not, I can't say for sure, it all depends on your luck."

Some even say:

"Please don't be anxious. You can't rush this. It depends on the opportunity, on the opportunity."

"Don't say you've been unemployed for a year, some people have been unemployed for two or three years and still haven't found anything."

Even more directly refuse.

"Please forgive me! My own position is a bit shaky right now."

"I don't think there's a way. If there were, why wouldn't I try to help you? There are still layoffs here, still layoffs!"

Each time he received such an answer, all his hopes were shattered; he dragged his body back dejectedly, knowing that the travel expenses were wasted again. And for an unemployed person, how much of a loss are these meager travel expenses!

"For me, one copper is worth more than a silver dollar! More! " he shouted angrily when he returned.

But what could he do? If he didn't try, the opportunity would never suddenly fall into his lap, but each blow made his heart sink lower. And now, after too many blows, his vision was almost completely dark.

The replies from afar also arrived one by one. But what were they? It was just another set of perfunctory, or even apologetic, letters! Even more disheartening, some people didn't even reply, making him long for a response and feel extremely annoyed!

So, the items in the house were almost all pawned off, and borrowing had reached the point where it was almost impossible to borrow any more. The family lived frugally, but it was still difficult to satisfy the daily need for rice, and the desire to find a job became more and more urgent; finding a job seemed to become more and more distant.

He tried his best to find "recruitment" or "employment" advertisements in the newspapers, but each time he read them, he felt discouraged. What "two hundred yuan deposit," what "famous person's introduction or guarantee," etc. So, each time, he would angrily throw the newspaper away or tear it up.

"If I had two hundred yuan, if I knew a famous person, how would I be afraid of being unemployed!" he shouted. A dark shadow floated in his heart.

He also went to employment agencies to register, filled out long forms, or talked sincerely with the staff. But what use is sincere conversation to an unemployed person?

"We will definitely notify you when there is an opportunity," the staff told him.

However, the notification was long, long overdue. Later, there was a notification, but after contacting them, either he was not qualified, or the conditions were too harsh. He qualified for two jobs, and the conditions had already been agreed upon, waiting only for the final decision ("How wonderful!" Now there are two opportunities, this time I won't be disappointed, he thought.) But on the day of signing the contract, an employee of one agency told him in the morning:

"I'm sorry! Our agency has suddenly suffered an unexpected blow and we don't need anyone right now! It's so difficult to get things done these days!"

And in the afternoon, an employee of another introduction agency noti

Page 20

fied him:

"Mr. Liu Jin: That position has already been taken by someone else. There are so many unemployed people now! So many! Those who are a little lacking are really being wronged!"

Then the whole world collapsed before Liu Jin's eyes, and his eyes blurred!

"Let me die! Let me die! This world! This world!" he shouted angrily, thinking of his family starving, and couldn't help but shed tears.

Summer Brothels 191

— Shi Dai

Yantai is a bustling city on the Bohai Sea coast. In summer, this place is called a "summer resort." In fact, it is true. As soon as it gets hot, the wealthy people double in number, and the prosperity of the market naturally has a new turn. I have stayed here twice before, but they were all violent winters with wind and snow, and the time was not long. At that time, Yantai gave me the impression that the time was not long. At that time, Yantai gave me the impression of angry sea waves, refugees begging from afar, groups of slaves whipped by hunger, and the miserable scene caused by the cold, all of which were heartbreaking. This is the third time I have come to this place. Because it is summer, the face of this city presents a different form. The sky is hanging with a scorching sun, and the red-roofed foreign houses and cement roads are scorching hot. Carts from the countryside are constantly walking around, and the mules pulling the carts are sweating profusely. Dirty dock coolies sweating with sweat are busy transporting goods under the scorching sun. The sea is so calm, and small motorboats, like flying birds, are running freely on the sea. American sailors, all white, are singing songs, as if deliberately mocking the sampan men.

There are quite a few people who put their hopes in the summer season. They are looking forward to the arrival of American warships and the start of all the seasonal businesses. Dance halls, Western restaurants, cafes, flower shops, and fruit companies have everything that American sailors and other vacationers need. As a result of their lifestyle habits, the people of Yantai do not feel threatened by the thirty or forty warships staying in the harbor. They always say that they are here to "rest" (note: meaning "summer resort"). After all, it is an infringement of our freedom. Why do they casually station warships in our harbor? The people of Yantai seem to be unclear about these things. They only know that "summer is here and they can earn money from foreigners."

In summer, Yantai is almost like a colony. The bloodstains of trampled slaves are everywhere, and as long as you are not deaf, you can still hear the roars of the hungry. The prostitutes in the "summer brothels" are slaves who are forced by life to sell their bodies. Every night I walked from the street under Yantai Mountain to the back coast. From this street, you can see countless "summer brothels." They do business entirely with foreigners. In other words, they are here for American sailors. If you pay a little attention while walking on this street, you will see those flamboyantly dressed Cantonese prostitutes and those drunk foreign sailors. I thought about going to the brothel to see it a few times, but I never mustered up the courage. So I only looked at the exterior when I passed by at night, but I really wanted to know the content of their lives. So I went to ask a friend who had been to the "summer brothel." That friend worked in a British foreign firm. Because he had money, he often went to brothels. I couldn’t bear to witness that tragic scene, so I quietly walked to the rocks and sat down to rest, looking at the star-like lights on the warships in the sea, and huge shadows moving on the water. The coolies’ cries coming from the west wharf were so beautiful.

——Hey! ——Suddenly someone patted my shoulder——When did you come?

It was Mr. Sun Weimin, the friend I mentioned who worked in a British firm. Behind him was a woman, whose face I could not see in the dark. When she sat on the rock next to me, I saw her dress from the shadows. Obviously she was a prostitute, and the style of her clothes was clearly from the "summer brothel."

The three of us sat on the rock and started chatting. Weimin likes to joke, and his speech is always humorous. We talked about the stars and the moon, and then we talked about the sea. The woman spoke:

——The sea looks cute now, but I am afraid of the sea. The year before last, my mother took me to Hong Kong from Xiamen, and she died by throwing herself into the sea. Last year, when I came to Yantai from Hong Kong, I encountered wind and waves again, which made me dizzy and almost die. Alas, I am really afraid of the sea. Why did someone invent trains and airplanes, but no one invented machines to fill the sea!

In the course of the conversation, she revealed her life story, and I took the opportunity to ask about the situation in their "summer brothel."

——Sir! Everyone says that we people in this line of work have no conscience, which is too wrong. We can't control our own bodies. We have to do whatever the madam tells us to do. She is for money, and what about us? We are the tools for her to make money. It is really extremely difficult for us to come to Yantai to do this three-month business. You can't do it if you can't speak English, and you can't do it if you can't sing foreign songs. The brothels here in Yantai (Note: That is, summer brothels) are all opened by Cantonese people, and the sisters are also Cantonese. They usually work in Hong Kong, Guangzhou, and Shanghai; when summer comes, they rush to this place. Alas! Those foreign sailors are too fierce, and they beat the sisters at every turn. No one wants to receive foreigners! ……”

The boundless night was floating on the sea. The warships were signaling SLE... The sound of the tide hitting the rocks and the roar of the ship's whistle suppressed the sound of the sampan's oars. We left the coast, and Weimin and the prostitute went back. I went to sleep. When I returned home, the apprentices were talking about the foreign sailors beating the prostitute to death.

Opening Chapter "Peach Blossom Spring"

Where is the fairy source to escape tea? In ancient times, there was a Wuling man who explored the secluded place. He was a fisherman who was leisurely in his profession. He came and went frequently on a boat of smoke and waves. He forgot how far or near the journey was. He only cared about going forward along the green stream. Suddenly, he saw peach blossoms on both sides of the bank that were redder than brocade. The reeds on the embankment were as green as grass. At the end of the forest, a good mountain rose up to meet him. The entrance of the cave was bright. The fisherman abandoned his boat and went ashore. He walked into the village through the peach blossoms. The fields were crisscrossed with mulberry and bamboo trees. The crowing of chickens and the barking of dogs could be heard in the distance. The men and women in the fields were dressed in ancient clothes. Suddenly, they met and laughed affectionately. The elderly and the young all looked happy. They killed chickens and made food to feast on the guests. They said that their ancestors had fled from the Qin Dynasty and lived in seclusion here. Today, they do not know what world it is, as if they are cut off from the mortal world. The fisherman described the events of today in detail. They sighed at the changes in the world. They prepared wine and food and invited him to stay. They were very kind to each other. The fisherman returned after several days. They all said, "Do not tell the outside world about this encounter." The fisherman returned to his boat and marked the original road. He told the governor to come to the stream. He left people to follow and explore again, but the entrance to the cave was gone. The virtuous scholar Liu Ziji from Nanyang was also in vain. From then on, no one asked about it again.

He Yunfang, He Qin, Double Pearls

Linji (1220) 11:15 AM to 12:00 PM

Opening Chapter "Pipa of Xunyang"

Sima Xiangshan went down to Jiangzhou. He stayed overnight at the ancient head of Xunyang Ferry. He sent off guests sadly and said goodbye. The reed flowers and maple leaves were in the late autumn of the river. I thought to myself, "I am sad that I have been exiled like a floating weed." The ancestor sent me off to board the boat on the water. Looking at the moon in the middle of the river, it was already the second watch when the watchtower was set up. Suddenly, I heard the sound of decay and the strings were plucked. Why is it so desolate that it seems to be complaining? Therefore, the host and guests searched for the sound and were close to the neighboring boat. They called him to move the boat to see each other, and he was half shy. Seeing that Qiu Niang was old but still charming, she added a pot of wine to the table. I only heard that she narrated her life and lingered in old dreams. But how could the spring flowers and autumn moon not stay again? The Kun string was pressed on the silver armor. Who knew that the mandarin duck tent was empty and the jade hook fell. The past is unbearable to look back on. There are endless stories from the bottom of my heart. Seeing that she was. There was only hatred left in the residual grease and powder. The blood-stained pomegranate skirt. Later, the carriages and horses gradually became scarce and desolate. How could she marry a husband from Fuliang and go and stay? It was like an autumn wind discarding the palace silk fan. It is difficult to invite the jade axe to repair the missing moon. It is known that the ancient Huanxi is the same as the officialdom. The vicissitudes of life have changed over the long years. I am also a wanderer in the world. I advise you to play another song and ask for more. It is all because I have nothing to give to you, so I will make a new tune and sing to repay you. When the song is over and the wine is gone and people are gone. A cry of the road back is heard. I only feel that red pink and blue tears are flowing.

Zhou Zhenyu - Righteous Demon Biography

Yuanchang (1120) Midnight 0:45 to 1:30 AM

Opening "Feng Huan of Qi" (Mimi Collection Listed Number) Feng Huan of Qi was poor and of humble origins. He once visited Lord Mengchang. He went to the door with a card in hand. After a brief exchange of pleasantries, he asked for his name. He was embarrassed by his shabby clothes and appearance. The guest was neither good nor capable. Knowing that you are generous and righteous, I am willing to be one of the three thousand retainers. He had already divided the houses into three classes, upper, middle, and lower. In the end, Lord Mengchang loved his guests. When he was idle, he leaned against the pillar and strummed his sword three times. When eating, there was no fish, and when going out, he had no carriage. Moreover, he had no food or clothing for his family. The generous Tian Wen did not refuse. He proudly told his neighbors. One day, he went to collect debts in the snow. Naturally, Mr. Feng Huan worked hard. He falsely conveyed an imperial decree, burned the contracts, and rewarded the poor people with beef and wine. He returned empty-handed to report. He made a name for you by buying righteousness. Unexpectedly, the King of Qi took back the prime minister's seal. The elders in Xue thanked him deeply. Feng Huan went to the state of Qin to persuade. He talked eloquently, and every sentence was listened to. He hired Tian Wen with high carriages and four horses. The state of Qi respectfully hired him from the state of Qin. He was still the prime minister in the court. Feng Huan's power brought half a lifetime of wealth. The three thousand retainers were difficult to judge. His wisdom and resourcefulness surpassed the past and the present.

Extra Notes

The Minyin Harmonica Society, organized by harmonica veterans Zhang Zhiren and scholars Chen Tianying and Zhao Jianqing, caused a sensation in Shanghai. Since April 10, when the main members of the society, Zhao Jianqing, Chen Tianying, etc., went to Suzhou for collective training, the special program has been suspended. It is now reported that the training period has expired, and they returned to Shanghai on the 10th of this month. It is expected that they will broadcast special programs on major radio stations soon, and it is believed that they will have better results and be heard by people from all walks of life.

The Yuanchang Broadcasting Station at No. 7, Sanrang Lane, Caishi Road, Shanghai, recently added a wireless radio repair department to meet the needs of listeners, specializing in repairing all kinds of wireless radios, with low prices, reliable projects, and fast delivery. For telephone notification, please call 82985. The station will send an engineer for free inspection upon receiving the call.

Huguang Weekly Postponed Publication 196

Since its publication, the Huguang Weekly has been warmly welcomed by readers in this city and other cities. The fourth issue was originally scheduled to be published on the 10th, but due to an unexpected incident between the journal and the printing house, it could not be published as scheduled. The fourth issue of the journal is now approved for publication on the 22nd of this month. The content is better than before, and the printing is exquisite and spectacular. There are more than 40 copperplate illustrations, and the cover is Shao Meiling, a dance star from Dahu Garden, specially printed in three-color collotype. Major dance halls, major theaters, and news vendors are all acting as sales agents.
